1935.04.08

Yellow Emperor Mausoleum Ceremony: National Tomb Sweeping Held, Central Representatives Preside, Solemn and Grand Ceremony, Zhang Shao et al. to Pay Respects at Zhou and Mao Mausoleums Tomorrow 1

(Xi'an) Yaoxian, 7th—The National Tomb Sweeping Ceremony was held at the Yellow Emperor Mausoleum in central Shaanxi at 8:00 AM on the 7th. Approximately 5,000 local people attended. Central representatives Zhang Ji, Shao Yuanchong, and Deng Jiayan presided over the ceremony, offering incense and flowers and reading the memorial address. Next, Shaanxi Province representatives Shao Lizi, Guo Yingfu, Feng Qinzao, and three others paid their respects and fired ceremonial cannons. The ceremony concluded at 9:00 AM, and the attendees then made a circle of obeisance around the Yellow Emperor Mausoleum. The ceremony was solemn and grand. At 9:30 AM, the central representatives departed southward, arriving in Yaoxian at 5:00 PM. They are scheduled to tour the Yaoxian scenic spot of Yaowang Mountain on the morning of the 8th and then return to Xi'an. They will then accompany representatives from all walks of life in Xi'an to pay respects at the Zhou and Mao Mausoleums on the morning of the 9th, returning to Xi'an that day. (Central News Agency dispatch, 7th)

(Xi'an) Central Shaanxi, 6th—National Tomb Sweeping representatives Zhang Ji, Shao Yuanchong, and their party were held up by rain in Tongguan on the 5th. On the morning of the 6th, they departed Tongguan at 10:00 AM and arrived in central Shaanxi at 5:00 PM. At 8:00 AM on the 7th, they paid respects at the Yellow Emperor Mausoleum and held the tomb sweeping ceremony. After the ceremony, they headed south that day and stayed overnight again in Tongguan. They are scheduled to visit the Zhou and Mao Mausoleums in Xianyang and Xingping on the 8th. Representatives from all walks of life in the provincial capital will depart for the Zhou Mausoleum on the morning of the 8th to participate in the ceremony. (Central News Agency dispatch, 7th)

Zhu and Mao Continue Eastern Retreat, Guangxi Army Opens Fire to Intercept 2

(Hong Kong) Ye Zhao, 6th—Since October 1st of last year to March of this year, my division has seized a total of 1,200 pieces of bandit weaponry and killed over 500 bandits. (Special dispatch, 7th)

(Hong Kong) Wu Jianxiong returned to the province from Shaozhou on the 7th to meet with Chen Jitang. (Special dispatch, 7th)

Guiyang—The communist bandits in Guizhou Province are still retreating eastward, trying their best to avoid contact with the government forces. After being defeated near Xifeng, the bandits initially retreated southeast, then turned southwest, then again southeast, and then eastward to within 20 li of Guiding (transliteration). Hearing that government forces were stationed there, they turned northwest and fled, crossing the Wu River this morning. Many drowned. This group of bandits is now moving rapidly eastward, hoping to join forces with the bandit group led by He Long. The bandits are moving busily in the mountains, their purpose clearly being to avoid contact with government forces at all costs. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Li Zongbao Cables He Jian to Surrender 3

(Changsha) Li Zongbao cabled the province from Yongxing on the 3rd to surrender. The cable was sent on his behalf by the county government. The original cable is as follows: Chairman and concurrently Security Commander He Jun: I, Zongbao, was forced into the wrong path by the communist bandits when I was not yet a young man. Over the years, I have acted perversely and accumulated many faults. Later, I felt the errors of the communist bandits' policies and mourned the peril of the nation. I believe that if we want to save China, there is no other way than to follow the Three Principles of the People. I have repeatedly wanted to leave the Red Army and serve the country, but I have been hampered by the strict supervision of the communist bandits and the obstruction of outside news. Until now, there has been no suitable opportunity to fulfill my aspirations. I hope for your pardon. This time, thanks to the recruitment of your envoy, I, Zongbao, went through many twists and turns and dangers to finally lead a company out of the sea of bitterness on the 1st. I am grateful for the excellent treatment given by Staff Officer Yang and County Magistrate Wu, and I am deeply ashamed. Zongbao respectfully offers his hot blood and dares not fail to exhaust his strength to follow you and repay your kindness. My wishes are as follows: 1. I will always support the Chinese Kuomintang and be the vanguard in suppressing bandits and eliminating communism, and prepare for the struggle against foreign aggression. 2. I am willing to take responsibility for recruiting and pacifying the remaining bandits in the Xiangnan border area to stabilize the local area. With all my sincerity, I humbly beg for your inspection and instructions. Li Zongbao bows respectfully. (Central News Agency dispatch, 6th)

Third Route Army Pays Respects to Fallen Soldiers 4

(Jinan) At noon on the 6th, the Third Route Army paid respects to the fallen soldiers of past years at the Martyrs' Shrine in Xinzhuang. Representatives from various agencies were sent to the ceremony. Han presided over the ceremony in person. After the ceremony, Han convened officers above the rank of major for instruction. (Central News Agency dispatch, 6th)

Fujian Provincial Committee, Lin Zhiyuan Arrives in Beijing Yesterday, Discusses Recent Situation in Fujian and Xiamen 5

(Nanjing) Lin Zhiyuan of the Fujian Provincial Committee arrived in Beijing on the morning of the 7th to discuss approximately two tasks: (1) To ask Chairman Lin to change the Fuzhou Mingluntang into a Zhongshan Hall. After President Sun Yat-sen resigned as Provisional President, he went to Fuzhou, where he gathered comrades and the masses in the province to explain his doctrine. This hall has been one of the places where the revolution originated. After years of disrepair, Chairman Lin once proposed rebuilding it as a Zhongshan Hall. Through the efforts of provincial and local figures, approximately 50,000 yuan has been raised, but the total construction cost is still insufficient. It is proposed to ask the central government for a small subsidy. (2) The budget for education expenses in Fujian Province is 1.44 million yuan per year. This sum is transferred from the salt tax to the national treasury and then allocated by the national treasury. Later, due to bandit and communist disturbances, the salt tax revenue fell short, and only 110,000 yuan was issued each month. At that time, the bandit areas had not been recovered, and the number of schools had decreased, so it could barely be maintained. Now, the counties in eastern, western, and northern Fujian have all been recovered, and the salt tax has returned to its original state, and the expenditure on education has also returned to its original state. The Education Expense Management Committee has pushed for a trip to Beijing, requesting the central government to continue allocating 120,000 yuan per month for education expenses in the entire province. He had an appointment with Finance Minister Kong in Shanghai, and they will meet in Beijing next Tuesday to discuss the matter face-to-face. After meeting with Chairman Chiang and Finance Minister Kong, he will stay in Beijing for a week and then return to Fujian. Fujian's political situation is gradually getting on the right track. After Chairman Chen took office, he managed it in stages. The first stage, in 1934, was dedicated to stability work. The second stage, in 1935, which is this year, is dedicated to rectification work. The third stage, in 1936, is dedicated to construction work. Stability work has been effective, and rectification work is underway. It is expected that there will also be satisfactory results by the end of the year. The financial situation has improved compared to before. The total annual expenditure of the province is approximately 20 million yuan, and the revenue is over 18 million yuan, with a deficit of only over 2 million yuan. The largest expenditure is the security expenses of the entire province, which requires 5 million yuan. The Director of Finance originally intended to tighten security expenses to match revenue and expenditure, but Chairman Chen is hesitant, fearing that tightening will affect stability work. Director Xu is currently traveling from Shanghai to Zhenhai and will come to Beijing in a day or two. As for the use of the 8 million yuan of construction bonds issued, 3 million yuan will be used for construction and the remaining 5 million yuan will be used to consolidate the old debts of the provincial treasury. Negotiations are currently underway. The atmosphere of bandits in Fujian is now cleared in eastern and northern Fujian, with only scattered remnants of bandits in western Fujian, which will not be difficult to eliminate. Order has also been restored in various places, but the vitality of the people needs considerable time to recover. The opium dens and gambling houses run by Taiwanese in Fuzhou have been negotiated to be banned. As a result, Fuzhou ordered all of them to close by the end of March. Due to various reasons, Xiamen has not yet achieved the purpose of banning them, but it is being done gradually. The Japanese Navy is also largely unsympathetic to the corrupt businesses run by the Taiwanese. However, the three powers of opium, gambling, and prostitution in the local area are completely in the hands of the Taiwanese, and it is expected that the prospect of banning them is still difficult. Many Chinese who run opium businesses use Taiwanese signs, even buying Taiwanese nationality with money as a protective charm for their business. There are no cases of false nationality in brothels, but the flower tax levied is too heavy. Prostitutes have to pay two yuan in flower tax for a ticket, but their income is only five yuan. Taiwanese brothels do not pay any taxes, so Chinese prostitutes cannot survive in Xiamen. After Xiamen was established as a city, Mayor Wang Guipan took office on the 1st of this month and plans to make a lot of efforts to reorganize the city. In the future, direct negotiations may be convenient, and it will not be necessary to transfer matters to the provincial government for resolution as before. (Special dispatch, 7th)

He Yaotsu Arrives in Shanghai to Wait for Ship to Go Abroad, Warm Farewell from Muslim Community 6

(Nanjing) He Yaotsu has completed the procedures for going to the United States and is scheduled to leave the country on the Italian ship Conte Verde on the 10th. Now that the ship's departure is approaching, he left Nanjing by train for Shanghai at 5:00 PM on the 7th. Lu Chao, Chen Diaoyuan, Tang Youren, Cao Haosen, Gu Zhenglun, Zou Zuocao, and approximately dozens of staff members from the two military departments all went to the Xiaguan Railway Station to see him off. The entire staff of the Beijing Muslim Association also gathered at the station to wave flags and send him off, which was extremely enthusiastic. He and his wife and entourage arrived at the station, and He repeatedly nodded to the people seeing him off, thanked them one by one, and the Muslim community set off firecrackers to send him off. He immediately boarded the train and went east amidst the sound of firecrackers. It is reported that after He arrives in Shanghai, he will hold a banquet for the press on the evening of the 8th and take a ship abroad with embassy staff on the 10th. (Central News Agency dispatch, 7th)

(Beiping) Zhang Zhitan previously suffered a stroke. After medical diagnosis and treatment, his body is still numb. According to the doctor, he needs long-term rest and has requested to resign as a member of the Political Reorganization Committee. (Central News Agency dispatch, 7th)

(Beiping) Regarding the issue of newly compiled security teams entering the war zone, it is reported that after careful consultation, the original Liu Zuozhou and Zhao Lei's departments stationed in the Yu area will increase their quotas. The two departments originally had more than 500 people in total and will be expanded to 1,000. Zhao Lei's department will be transferred to Fengrun. Yang Bencheng's department of the Hebei Provincial Security Team will be stationed in Lulong Zhenning to maintain law and order. (Special dispatch, 7th)

(Tianjin) The original Zhou Yuying department stationed in Funing will be transferred to Yutian, Zhao Lei's department will be transferred to Run, and Yang Yucheng's department will be stationed in Lulong. The area along Zunhua, Funing, Yuguan, Tangshan, and Changli will all be defended by the new security teams. (Special dispatch, 7th)

(Beiping) It was telegraphed from Zunhua that the remnants of bandits entrenched in Shenshentai Liuxingyu were surrounded and suppressed by local militias, killing more than 20 people. On the 6th, all fled north. (Central News Agency dispatch, 7th)

Violent Wind and Rain in Eastern Tianjin 11

(Tianjin) Eastern Tianjin has been experiencing continuous storms and rain. At 1:00 PM on the afternoon of the 5th, a violent wind blew, with flying sand and stones. In the area of Qixin Yanghui Company on West Ma Road in Tangshan, many trees in the open fields were blown down. On the afternoon of the 6th, rain fell and thunder rumbled, and it only cleared up at night. The roofs of houses in the Baoshenmiao area were blown away by the wind. Many railway houses and trees were broken. Countless power lines were broken in the city. Westbound trains were delayed. Spring wheat and vegetable seedlings were severely damaged. The waves in the river were two feet high, and two fishing boats capsized. (Special dispatch, 7th)

Three-Level, Three-Trial System to Be Implemented in Fourteen Provinces in the First Phase 15

(Nanjing) Of the provinces and regions that have previously decided to implement the three-level, three-trial court organization law in the first phase, Shandong, Anhui, and Hubei are the three provinces. It is now reported that Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shanxi, Hebei, Henan, Hunan, Jiangxi, Guangdong, Guangxi, Fujian, and Gansu are also in the planning, totaling as many as fourteen provinces. The Ministry of Justice has also issued an order to the above-mentioned provinces, limiting them to respond within twenty days of receipt of the document, whether it can be implemented as scheduled, so as to decide everything. In addition, after the implementation of the three-level, three-trial system, all third-level trials in the country will be handled by the Supreme Court. The court currently has civil and criminal divisions, and it will be necessary to increase the number of divisions according to actual needs in order to handle the cases. As for how many new divisions should be added, it has not yet been decided and is being discussed by the Ministry of Law and the Supreme Court. (Central News Agency dispatch, 7th)

Current Affairs Commentary

Thoughts and Hopes on the Reading Movement 61

— Hua

There is a Western proverb that says, "Knowledge is power." This saying is indeed true. In terms of an individual, a person lacking knowledge cannot undertake important tasks because of insufficient ability. Extending this to the entire society and nation, if scholars do not enjoy learning and the majority of the people are ignorant, then society will inevitably become numb and apathetic, and the national spirit will inevitably wither and decline. It would be difficult to expect it to be strong and powerful. An ancient person said, "Lack of soldiers is not a cause for deep concern; lack of provisions is not a cause for bitter weeping. The only thing to be concerned about is looking at this world and seeking someone who rushes to seize profits without first fulfilling his duty, and who fears being behind in loyalty and righteousness. Such a person is not readily found. This is something to lament greatly." Our country is in a dangerous international environment today. Dare we rephrase it? The oppression of foreign aggression is not a cause for deep fear; the impact of the economic panic and the tide of chaos is not a cause for deep concern. Only the weakness of the intelligence of our entire nation is insufficient to cope with the various difficult and complex internal and external problems, making my society and country embark on a bright way out, which is truly regrettable. Reading is a way to increase knowledge. If we want to remedy the problem of insufficient general intelligence in our country, we cannot but hope that students will read more, and that all literate people will also read more, using reading as a method to achieve the purpose of increasing knowledge. Now, for the purpose of enriching the national intelligence, the China Cultural Construction Association has launched a national reading movement and is holding a national reading competition, setting up registration offices in the provincial and municipal branches of the Cultural Construction Association (the details of which are detailed in the education news of this newspaper on March 26). It stipulates that the first reading period is from April 1 to the end of September. The association also prepares a bonus of 3,000 yuan to reward those who achieve excellent results in order to encourage them. This kind of movement and method really meets the needs of China today. "Starting is simple, finishing is huge." We deeply hope that it can produce great effects in the future.

The Reading Competition, in its first reading period, corrects the shortcomings of today's school system in a negative way, and cultivates a national atmosphere of love of learning in a positive way. We dare to believe that it should be helpful. However, there are many illiterate people in our country and very few good popular readings. In addition, relatively complete libraries are limited to a few large cities. If we want the effectiveness of the Reading Competition to increase and the practical effect of the reading movement to be universal throughout the country in the future, then the advancement of illiteracy eradication, the compilation of popular readings, and the expansion and addition of libraries must be carried out simultaneously. We secretly hope that the people of the country will also pay attention to and work hard on this.

At present, students and those who can participate in the Reading Competition are fortunate in terms of the comparison of the level of knowledge with the general illiterate. Therefore, we hope that on the one hand, we will read more books, and on the other hand, we will observe and study our entire society as a book. Do not adhere to the old and conservative, do not blindly follow suit, understand the real needs of today's society and country, and work hard. When research is successful, further uphold the principle of "establishing oneself and establishing others," and do our best to provide assistance to those with a lower level of knowledge. This is also our hope for students across the country and all those participating in the competition.

Congress Passes US President's Public Works Relief Bill Dedicated to Relieving Unemployed People Intense Debate During Discussion 63

(Washington) Congress today passed President Roosevelt's $4.88 billion public works relief bill. The government has also immediately planned to create jobs for 3.5 million unemployed people. There was intense and lengthy debate when the two houses finally passed the bill. The president even lost control of the Senate Democrats three times. However, the power granted to the president by the bill was greater than his original proposal. The president is now free to dispose of a portion of the funds for agricultural adjustment purposes. In this way, if the government deems it appropriate, all business taxes can be abolished. $880 million of the funds will be controlled by Federal Relief Bureau Director Hopkins and will still be used for direct relief to unemployed people. However, the president hopes that after the government employs a large number of people, the need for direct relief can be gradually reduced. The large amount of funds allocated by the bill is unprecedented in the United States in peacetime, and the president has the power to dispose of it freely. It is said that the president was very pleased to hear that the bill had passed. He has repeatedly said that if 5 million unemployed people in the United States regain their jobs, the US depression can be eliminated. Now that the bill has been passed, according to the methods it stipulates, the government must find a way to use at least one-third of the funds as wages, and there are no other restrictions. The various amendments proposed by the two houses during the discussion were not passed. (6th National Telegram)

US House Passes Wartime Military Service Personnel Increased to 23 Million People 64

(Washington) The House of Representatives today passed a bill increasing the total number of military personnel serving in the United States during wartime to 23 million. This bill is an amendment to the McSwain War Profits Cancellation Act. There was almost no opposition when it was voted on. Its content is to change the originally stipulated military service age from 21 to 31 years old to 21 to 45 years old. In addition, McSwain's proposal also has four amendments that have been passed as follows: (1) All "excessive" profits during wartime must be fully paid as national taxes. (2) Authorize the government to confiscate all domestic resources. (3) Guarantee that army and navy personnel receive wages equal to the minimum wage of unskilled workers. (4) Prohibit American soldiers from fighting in foreign countries. In the future, the American army can only defend American territory. (6th National Telegram)

Holland Maintains Gold Standard; Content of Franco-Belgian Trade Agreement; In the Future, Belgian Cargo Ships to France Will Be Priced in Francs; Has Been Approved by the Governments of Both Countries, Term Limit is Six Months 68

(Paris) The Cabinet today approved the Franco-Belgian trade agreement. The agreement was drafted yesterday by French Minister of Commerce Marchandeau and Belgian Prime Minister Chierante in Brusel. (6th National Telegram) The Franco-Belgian trade agreement in Brussels was approved by the Belgian Cabinet today. (6th National Telegram)

(Paris) The main contents of the trade agreement established yesterday between France and the Belgium-Luxembourg Economic Union are as follows: The governments of Belgium and Luxembourg, in view of the fact that Belgian goods may flood into the French market after the devaluation of currency, and that their low prices are sufficient to disrupt the French economy, have decided to take various beneficial measures to prevent this. This decision has been filed by the French government. The governments of France and Belgium have decided on the following points:

(1) Groups composed of producers of certain goods on both sides have reached an understanding, and this understanding has been recognized by both governments. They should be ordered to compromise with each other and take necessary restrictive measures. If these groups cannot reach a compromise, the governments of both sides should take necessary measures.

(2) For goods imported into France that are subject to quota restrictions, the seller should declare in writing that the price sold should not be lower than the usual price (the so-called usual price is the price before the devaluation of the Belgian currency), and then the French government will issue an import license. Violators will be prohibited from importing for a period of one year.

(3) For other goods, when necessary, the governments of Belgium and Luxembourg will be responsible for establishing a license system and conducting audits to ensure that the price of these goods imported into France is not lower than the usual price due to the devaluation of the Belgian currency.

(4) France and the Belgium-Luxembourg Economic Union should immediately hold commercial negotiations based on this concrete approach.

(5) The term of validity of the above agreement is limited to six months. The two governments can adjust the prices of goods on their own. If they are satisfied, they can announce the termination before the expiration date. (6th Havas Telegram)

(Paris) After the devaluation of the Belgian currency, the prices of goods from this country calculated in French francs have become cheaper than before. Therefore, the French market has a place for Belgian goods to be dumped. In order to prevent this, the commercial authorities of France and Belgium signed a compromise this afternoon after very friendly negotiations. According to this agreement, Belgian goods imported into a certain country should not be lower in price than when the Belgian currency was not devalued without sufficient reason, and the amount of French goods imported into Belgium should not be reduced compared to before. In the future, Belgian goods imported into France will be priced in French francs. (6th Reuters

Dutch Currency Stable

Hague: Semi-official sources believe that there is no need to worry about the future of the Dutch currency. The speculator's short selling movement has now stopped. The National Bank's discount rate, which was previously increased from 2.5% to 3.5% on Thursday, has taken effect and is sufficient to prevent cash from flowing abroad. The government and the National Bank authorities have decided to maintain the current monetary policy and will use all means to prevent the Dutch currency from falling. It is generally believed that the impact of the Belgian currency devaluation has reached its peak and there is no risk of contagion. The Dutch currency will still follow the French franc, in other words, maintain the gold standard. (6th Havas Telegram)

The Hague, capital of the Netherlands: The Dutch Telegraph Agency said that after the National Bank increased the discount rate from 2.5% to 3.5% on Thursday, it was originally scheduled to increase it again yesterday. Although cash is still being continuously shipped to the United States at this time, financial figures believe that the future of the Dutch currency will not change. Even if speculators continue to manipulate it, the Netherlands will still maintain the current parity. Germany Develops Audacious New Weapons: Five Types Including Stratosphere Rockets and Rotating Cannons; Secret Rays Can Destroy Aircraft and Armored Vehicles 73

(London) The Sunday Chronicle reports that in the past fifteen years, German technicians have invented five types of new weapons that are extremely frightening, namely: (1) Bullets that can penetrate all obstacles, called "the latest Hohlkern," invented by Max Orr. 480,000 of these bullets can be manufactured every day. (2) Krupp's rotating cannon, which has five rotating weapons inside and can fire 1,000 shells in one minute. 2,000 units have already been manufactured. (3) Stratosphere rockets, which contain violent poison gas and can be controlled freely within a circle with a diameter of 320 kilometers. (4) Z-rays: the method of making them is absolutely secret. They form an invisible wall for France, bridges can be destroyed by them, gun emplacements can be melted, aircraft can disintegrate, radio stations can turn into ashes, and armor and railroads are also affected. (5) A bizarre machine gun weighing two kilograms that can fire 600 rounds per minute. In addition, there is a new type of heavy machine gun mounted on a car that can fire 1,400 bullets per minute. (Seventh Havas Dispatch)

Soviet Political Commentator Discusses the International Situation, Contributes Opinions on the Three-Nation Conference: Europe Stands at a Crossroads 74

(Moscow) The famous Soviet political commentator Radek has an article, "After a British Cabinet Member's Visit," published in Izvestia. Radek first quoted a dispatch from the London Times correspondent in Berlin, saying that Hitler will never convince British politicians that the Soviet Union poses any threat to Germany. Radek further stated that German diplomatic circles once regarded Simon and Eden as mediators between Germany and France, and that Germany could use them to make France realize that France has nothing to fear from Germany. Radek then quoted an article from the March 30th issue of the Journal de Genève to prove that the intensification of military preparations in East Prussia is merely a disguise, and that the actual goal of German policy is France and its allies. Radek further pointed out that all of Germany's demands regarding increasing its army, navy, and air force are primarily aimed at the Western powers. Regarding Germany's opposition to Eastern European treaties, what it opposes is not only the Soviet Union, but also Poland. Radek continued, "The British Cabinet members will report their observations to the government, and the inferences they make will certainly not be detrimental to the Soviet Union. At the same time, they must ease the impressions of Berlin and Moscow so that the door for negotiations between the countries will not be closed. However, the current issue is not to establish the situation that already exists, but to establish the situation that must be established. Therefore, the main issue at present should be as follows: Germany cannot satisfy its demands after a war of fire. Today, Germany is again relying on its military power to make its demands. Currently, from a military point of view, Germany's economic resources are very limited and are still weaker compared to countries willing to maintain peace. However, today's Europe is clearly standing at a crossroads. If some individuals are given freedom, then the situation will develop towards military alliances and war. The second path is to reconsider and try to establish new relations of power in Europe after considering the existing changes. The European powers are now facing a problem, namely, reorganizing the League of Nations to make it consistent with the new relations of power. At the same time, if we wish to avoid a future world war, the League of Nations can settle some issues in an amicable manner so that they can be left unresolved. Is this method possible?" Radek reiterated the suggestion of strengthening Articles 10 and 16 of the League of Nations Covenant, saying that these articles had no power before the Manchurian Incident, so all those who cherish peace will certainly not oppose their revision. "However, we must remember that in the past, countries also wanted to accomplish this by specifying the general provisions of the Covenant. The League of Nations accepted the so-called Geneva Protocol proposed by France, but the British government did not ratify it because the constraints it listed were too strict. Conversely, the British government put forward its Western Regional Pact based on a concept, namely, that the major powers are more likely to accept certain definite obligations for certain definite issues, while these obligations do not bind the whole world, but bind a specific region. This pact was solemnly pointed out in the Anglo-French proposals of February 3, its Western Sky Pact, which stipulates that any Western European country that encounters an attack must immediately provide sky-based assistance. The Eastern European Mutual Assistance Regional Pact proposed by France and the Soviet Union is based on the belief that obligations that are accurately defined for certain specific and complex issues must be easier to accept than obligations to the entire world. Although we have encountered opposition from Germany and Poland, we are convinced that this viewpoint is not wrong. We believe that we must not lose heart in the face of difficulties. On the contrary, we will fight to overcome the difficulties. We must specifically consider where the danger zones that threaten peace are, which regional pacts are necessary, and at the same time, how to link them into an organization and insert them into the League of Nations Covenant. When the major powers consider the issue of defining the meaning of the League of Nations Covenant, they must also study other issues that are more concerning to other countries, especially the meaning of Article 19 of the Covenant (regarding the amendment of treaties that have become invalid and threaten war). "The Soviet Union will take a favorable attitude towards the presentation of all issues that can strengthen peace. However, such issues may not be decided by the three countries meeting in Stresa, because they require the cooperation and exchange of views of all relevant countries. We must demand that the Stresa Conference not add obstacles to the path of universal decisions. On the contrary, it must promote this work. The main task of the conference is to confirm that the situation studied by the British Cabinet members does not require the cancellation of the Anglo-French proposals of February 3, but is a resolute struggle to strive for their realization. In the current situation, if anyone believes that the problem of solving universal security can be achieved by concluding a sky mutual assistance pact in the West with Westerners, and the rest will be "continued efforts" (this is diplomatic language), then this decision will be detrimental to universal security. At the same time, a new situation will arise in European countries. It is not enough for us to only ask the Stresa Conference not to do harm. We must also demand that the representatives of the three major countries, with a calm and resolute attitude, convey the intentions of their respective governments to create a collective security organization. In this effort, they must consider the vigorous cooperation of the Soviet Union, which is as concerned as the other countries in maintaining peace, and which is less concerned than other countries about the work of isolating or discriminating against a certain country," he said. (Sixth TASS Dispatch)

However, whether the Seiyukai can accommodate or not is quite doubtful. (Seventh Denchu Dispatch)

American Poet Robinson Dies in Square Garden 88

(New York) Edwin Arlington Robinson, one of America's great modern poets, died here today at the age of sixty-five. Robinson attended Harvard University but did not graduate. He later moved to New York and devoted himself to various careers, serving as a clerk in the U.S. Customs. Before long, he gained fame as a poet and won the Pulitzer Prize for best poetry three times each year. (Sixth Reuters Dispatch)

German Air Force Expansion 93

— (German Dispatch)

Although Germany is restricted by the Treaty of Versailles, it is determined not to lag behind in the clamor for military expansion, especially in the armament of its air force. Even those who have been stationed here for a long time do not quite know how many airplanes Germany actually has. Conservative British leader Baldwin estimates there are between six hundred and one thousand. The French Minister of Aviation estimates there are one thousand one hundred. Ernst Henri, the author of "Will Hitler Conquer Europe?", says it has one thousand two hundred to one thousand five hundred. He also says that the current production capacity of all German aircraft factories, when fully mobilized, can produce two thousand airplanes per month. Although Germany is restricted by the treaty and cannot freely expand its air defense, it has devised another method, which is to develop civil aviation. Civil aviation is controlled by the Ministry of Aviation. For example, the overnight express train between Berlin and East Prussia has been discontinued since last year and replaced by air travel. Last year alone, the total distance of airline routes was six million miles, carrying one hundred thousand passengers and one million kilograms of cargo. The length of its routes is almost equal to the combined length of the airline routes of England, Italy, and the Netherlands. Under the command of German Aviation Minister Göring, there are now two large aircraft manufacturing factories, namely "Junkers" and "Dornier." They are currently building excellent commercial passenger aircraft, but with a quick turnaround, they can be converted into military aircraft, which has already been tested. The new "D-2000" model aircraft manufactured by "Dornier" can carry a load of five thousand kilograms, with a speed of two hundred and fifty kilometers per hour and a range of one thousand kilometers. For example, the "G-3 Hindenburg Marshal" also has the same payload characteristics, but it is also equipped with two twenty-millimeter cannons, a command tower, and several machine guns. This is truly an airborne flying warship.

If these types of aircraft are formed into a squadron, using two hundred to two hundred and fifty to form a team to fly from Hamburg to London, then the bombs dropped in one go could be equal to all the bombs dropped on London by German aircraft during the European War—eight hundred tons. And the losses suffered, if flying at night, the opposing anti-aircraft guns and anti-aircraft machine guns would lose their effectiveness, and their own losses would be at most a sacrifice of 15%.

We also know that the reason why it is not easy to expand the air force is not only in the manufacture of aircraft, but also, more importantly, in the training of pilots who can fly and accurately drop bombs. Germany currently has more than two thousand five hundred well-trained pilots. Due to the expansion of its domestic aviation network, they are familiar with the conditions in the skies above their country, its borders, and even other countries, as well as the geographical features, climate changes, and so on. In times of war, they can immediately become excellent pilots. According to Göring's plan, he will organize an airborne assault force of three hundred thousand people in the future. The first step of his aviation policy is to vigorously promote the necessity of air defense, so that the general public understands the great significance of air defense, and further arouse the public's interest in flying, and promote the aviation craze among young people. Ordinary aviation techniques are taught in all secondary schools, and the skill of piloting an airplane is transformed into a game. This policy has had considerable effect so far, and the students' enthusiasm for flying has indeed been aroused by his policy. Now they all want to engage in flying.

Göring's policy is not only for male students, but also extends to the women's community recently, so an women's department has been newly established in aviation schools, teaching them specialized knowledge of air defense. They are also taught about the effects of poisonous gas and the methods of detoxification and disinfection. In addition, there are various tasks, such as minimizing the spread of fire caused by incendiary bombs, temporary special treatment for the injured and poisoned, bandaging methods, and temporary rapid construction of shelters. Even the work of specialized scientists and carpenters must be learned by women. Currently, under the education department of the Air Defense Association, eight hundred women's associations have learned various air defense methods. This alone shows Germany's efforts in air defense and air force armament are fully loaded, which is truly unprecedented by others. Even on the locomotive hood, people sometimes climb and sit, and the co-driver stands on the footplate, letting one seat carry two passengers. The car is overloaded, which leads to dangers along the way, so the railway bureau should find ways to restrict it. If it can plan as a whole and organize strictly, and take all vehicles completely into public ownership, it will be more secure in terms of traffic safety.

After the snow, the reporter set off from Lanzhou. The weather was very sunny. The car started from the Grand Hotel outside the South Gate. Just as it was about to leave Dongshaomen, military police checked the luggage. Seeing a coffin placed under the car, transported from Xinjiang, they suspected it contained musk or valuables, but it was not convenient to open it for inspection. After a long time of investigation, they finally let it go. Among the crowd gathered nearby, a water carrier accidentally placed a cigarette butt in his pocket. His cotton-padded jacket was burned, and he screamed in pain. The gaze of the crowd's inspection was immediately focused on him. Seeing him hurriedly take off his jacket, smoke came out from the collar, and everyone couldn't help but laugh. A bucket of Yellow River water was placed nearby, and a thin layer of ice had just formed on the surface of the water. From this, one can see the coldness of spring in Lanzhou and prove the time-consuming nature of the inspection. There were also five special cargo trucks traveling with us. Each truck was carrying three soldiers and one or two freight merchants with yellow silk strips on their chests. The trucks had small flags of the Gansu Province Anti-Smoking Committee inserted on the front. They all passed us (the inspection point), not only without stopping, but also speeding away first. What exactly was loaded in the trucks? The inspectors probably knew at a glance.

The car left Lanzhou's Dongshaomen and traveled about seven or eight miles. The wind and dust were flying, making it difficult to breathe. The city tower with the atmosphere of an ancient capital and the beautifully scenic Five Springs Mountain were successively obscured and could not be looked back upon. There were barracks on the left side of the road, as large as a square city, with four gates opened facing south. Each gate had a screen wall in front of it, arranged in a straight line from east to west. Each wall had slogans written on it. Reading from east to west, they said "Revive the Chinese Nation," "Rectify Combat Readiness Actions," "Consolidate Northwest National Defense," "Recover the Lost Territories of the Northeast." The characters were in large fonts and clearly visible from a distance, with forceful tones. But what about implementing them? Twelve or thirteen miles to Donggang Slope, yellow slopes lined the road, winding slowly. Five miles to Yama's Ravine, the cliffs stood tall on the right, and the wells were deep and sunken on the left. The road was extremely narrow and dangerous, and robberies often occurred in the past. The cliffs were artificially cut, with green stones and yellow earth layered alternately, neatly and beautifully. The ravine was divided into three branches, and one of them was filled in, 120 meters high, which took more than 60,000 labor days and cost more than 10,000 silver dollars. When the car traveled here, it suddenly stopped. After a brief conversation with Mr. Someone from the Engineering Office, it was said that the construction of this ravine was done by a specially hired foreign engineer, otherwise there would be no such achievement. It was also said that the engineer's name was so-and-so, and that he was very friendly with him, and his words were quite complacent. Twenty miles to Zhujiazuizi (commonly known as Pig's Mouth), the mountains stretched far to the left, and the land was flat. Crossing the Majiasi River, the river water was frozen along the road, smooth and crystal clear, like crossing a jade bridge. Seventy miles to Gancaodian, there were more than four hundred households of residents, with earthen houses laid out flat, patches of residual snow, and several old trees, on which migratory birds with shrunken necks perched. The courtyards of the villages passed by were square and walled, with ancient moss and black spots on the northwest sides, while those facing southeast had no moss traces. Military science uses moss traces to identify directions, which can be said to be practical and based on evidence. After this, the journey became winding. The Baoweizhan's car ascended the first ridge, with high cliffs and deep valleys, allowing only one road to pass. In the past, the Ming general Xu Da defeated the Yuan bandit Wang Baobao at Chedao, which was located here. The terraced wheat fields on the mountain, along with the half-dissolved snow, contrasted the dark yin and the bright yang, creating an interesting scene. The farmers lived in caves dug out of the cliffs near their cultivated land, so there were no villages. Going downhill and crossing the stream, it was already night. There were very high ice ridges, and the car could not go up. Everyone got out of the car to pull it, but unexpectedly, bags and cushions fell into the water one after another. Everyone rolled up their sleeves and entered the water, stirring the ice and retrieving them, all exhaling and shivering. The reporter lost a map, which someone conveniently picked up, but it was covered in mud and sand and could no longer be used. Later, they traveled another thirty or forty miles at night and arrived at Dingxi City to stay. From Lanzhou to here, the distance was two hundred and forty miles, and the actual measurement was more than 113 kilometers. The hotel room had a round top and a square bottom, just like a kiln bridge, no different from living in a cave, called a cave dwelling. The walls and top were made of earth, cool in summer and warm in winter, but the light and air were quite lacking. Mr. Someone in the same car talked by the stove after dinner, discussing the lack of teachers in Lanzhou schools as follows:

There are many schools in Lanzhou, but the lack of teachers is particularly noticeable. Elementary schools are still flawless, but in secondary schools and above, the higher the grade, the more obvious the shortcomings. Gansu College, the highest institution of higher learning in Gansu Province, sometimes has more faculty members than students, but in terms of quality, it is absolutely impossible to compliment them. Moreover, one person teaches in four or five schools, with up to forty points of assigned classes per week, exceeding the number of class hours for students. Therefore, they often have to ask for leave or be absent from classes in rotation from various schools. Graduates who transfer to national universities as transfer students often have more than enough qualifications but insufficient level. Students from other counties who come to the province to take the entrance examination mostly take the entrance examination for the First High School first, followed by the First Normal School and the Fifth High School. If all three schools fail, they transfer to Gansu College with fake diplomas, and many are lucky enough to be admitted. The college fees are more than 90,000 yuan per year, and there is no lack of criticism in society. If the education authorities really want to strengthen rectification, they must break away from favoritism and eliminate the outdated, otherwise it will be difficult to achieve results.

Jiangxi Province Commemorates the Fallen Soldiers who Died, Held on the Qingming Festival 94

Nanchang dispatch: The Jiangxi Red bandits have been eliminated through five encirclements and suppressions by the central government with all its strength. It has been eight years since then. The number of fallen soldiers and murdered civilians is unknown. The Jiangxi Provincial People's Association and other groups initiated a large-scale memorial service, which was prepared for three months and held on the Qingming Festival. Representatives from various central agencies, provinces, counties, and cities participated in the memorial service. The details are as follows:

The memorial service was held at the newly completed Lishi Society. The society building, towering on the banks of the river, had colorful flower cloth arches erected on the main road in front, east and west. The passageway between the two arches was covered with elegiac couplets from various provincial, city, and county agencies and organizations. From a distance, it was a white expanse. At the entrance, there were three colorful arches, all with a solemn atmosphere. The auditorium was in the society's grand hall. Above it was the spirit tablet of the soldiers who died in the suppression of bandits in Jiangxi and the loyal martyrs who were martyred. In front was the main sacrificial platform, filled with incense, flowers, fruits, and offerings. Below were the seats for representatives from all walks of life, and the surrounding area was covered with eulogies and wreaths, which were extremely brilliant. On that day, the attendees included Cheng Tianfang from the Central Party Department, Gu Zhutong representing the Military Commission, Xue Yuesui representing the Executive Yuan, Xu Chonghao from the Examination Yuan, Lu Shizeng from the Judicial Yuan, Zheng Luosheng from the Control Yuan, Tu Weifan and other representatives from the military, naval, financial, and educational departments, Lin, Cheng Tianfang, Xu Shi, and other representatives from the provinces of Suiyuan, Jiangsu, Gansu, Fujian, Anhui, Shaanxi, Henan, Zhejiang, Shandong, Guangdong, various military divisions, and representatives from organizations and groups, totaling more than two thousand people. The participants all wore black gauze armbands. The ceremony was conducted by all in blue robes and black jackets, with the Central Party Department and ten other agencies forming the main sacrificial group.

At about 8:00 AM, the solemn and solemn opening ceremony began. Amidst the rumbling of cannons, mourning music was played, the flag was lowered to half-mast, and the rituals were performed. Chairman Yu Baiqing reported the significance of the meeting, stating that today is a day for the nation to sweep the tombs and commemorate the soldiers who died in the suppression of bandits and the loyal martyrs who were martyred, which is also a sacrifice for the revival of the nation, with great significance. He hoped that everyone would continue to work hard, sweep away the remaining bandits, and complete the work of revival. Next, the public memorial was held. Representatives from the Central Party Department, the National Government, the Military Commission, and other agencies offered sacrifices in turn, with the following rituals: (1) The chief officiant takes his place; (2) The participants take their places; (3) Mourning music is played; (4) Three bows are performed; (5) Wreaths are presented; (6) Libations are offered; (7) Fruits are offered; (8) The chief officiant retires; (9) The ceremony ends. From 1:00 PM to 3:00 PM, the Party, government, military, and police agencies held public sacrifices. From 3:00 PM to 5:00 PM, business and academic circles paid tribute. From 5:00 PM to 6:00 PM, mass organizations paid tribute.

There were no less than ten thousand elegiac couplets and eulogies from various places. The Central Party Department inscribed "Great Martyrs' Eternal Glory." Chairman Lin inscribed "Unyielding Heroic Spirits." Chairman Chiang's elegiac couplet read, "Pity the worms and sands in the dust, relying on your sacrifice for righteousness, jointly support justice, drum up thoughts for the soldiers, and see the remaining bandits about to be annihilated, enough to comfort the heroic spirits." President Wang's elegiac couplet read, "Stars and beautiful mountains leave their remaining brilliance, and wind and rain, the spiritual flag endows great recruitment." Zhang Xueliang's elegiac couplet read, "Peng Bo's clear report of virtue, Kuang Lu's fragrant atmosphere endows the call of souls." The rest are omitted.

It has been eight years since the suppression of the Red bandits in Jiangxi. The losses of the central government and local areas are no less than hundreds of millions. The division commanders who died include Hu Zuyu of the Fifth Division, Zhang Huizuan of the Eighteenth Division, Li Ming of the Fifty-second Division, and Guo Bingsheng of the New Thirty-sixth Division. There are also quite a few brigade and regimental commanders. Permanent monuments will be built to commemorate them forever. (April 6)

The Headquarters Announces Measures to Ban Opium and Drugs, Banning Drugs in Two Years and Opium in Six Years as Scheduled, Circulating Orders to the Provincial and Municipal Governments of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, and Other Provinces to Comply 95

Hankou dispatch: In order to strictly ban opium and drugs, the Headquarters of the Chairman of the Military Commission, in addition to the effective regulations promulgated by the former General Headquarters for the Suppression of Bandits in the Three Provinces, has formulated two implementation measures for banning drugs and opium, adding a concise outline and detailed and strict supplements, and further expanding the scope of implementation.
