Northwest Inspection Report 96

— By Our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya

On the Road Through Gansu and Shaanxi

The Xi'an-Lanzhou highway is still under construction, but commercial vehicles have been transporting goods and passengers between the two cities for years. This route is a vital transportation artery connecting Qin (Shaanxi) and Long (Gansu), impacting the prosperity of commerce in the Northwest. In the past, relay horse transportation was used, with eighteen horse stations. Now, by car, the journey takes five to six days. Once the entire line is completed, it is expected to be reduced to three to four days. However, currently, most of the vehicles operate as both passenger and freight carriers. There are as many as eighty or ninety car companies operating on the northern route. However, each company owns only one to three vehicles. The companies compete fiercely, arbitrarily lowering prices to attract customers. According to the Transportation Committee's designated price for the entire line, it should be over fifty yuan per passenger, but the actual ticket prices vary greatly. From Xi'an to Lanzhou, with congested freight, each ticket still sells for twenty-seven or twenty-eight yuan. From Lanzhou to Xi'an, with less freight, the ticket prices are even lower, sometimes selling for only fourteen or fifteen yuan. While this is economical for passengers, the passenger and freight

Page 10

provinces and municipal governments, 1. To comply with, now recording the orders of the Office of the Commander-in-Chief and the measures to prohibit opium and narcotics as follows:

Orders from the Office of the Commander-in-Chief: Upon investigation, the anti-opium affairs in the ten provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hunan, Shaanxi, and Gansu were entrusted to the Military Affairs Commission for handling in July of last year, according to the National Government's Order No. 480. Regarding the prohibition of opium and narcotics, the Commission referred to the effective measures for investigating and prohibiting opium and narcotics that were piloted by the General Headquarters of the Henan, Hubei, and Anhui provinces in the bandit suppression areas. Rules and regulations were formulated, strengthened, and enforced with military law, which has become increasingly effective since its implementation. In the provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangsu, even in remote areas, opium seedlings are rarely found. Furthermore, in the Jiangsu Province, the registration of opium addicts, which was organized by the provincial government last year, has achieved remarkable results in just a few months of management of smoking and sales. A provisional ordinance strictly prohibiting highly addictive drugs was also promulgated and implemented in provinces such as Hebei, Chahar, Suiyuan, and cities such as Peiping and Tianjin, and its strict enforcement has had a significant impact, rescuing people from misery and gaining international sympathy. However, in the past, the scourge of drugs and opium spread too widely. Now, to thoroughly eliminate and ban them as scheduled, it is necessary to take a further step, strictly defining the procedures so that the inland and remote provinces can advance simultaneously and equally. Otherwise, if the root source is not blocked, and efforts are relaxed in one area while strengthened in another, it will greatly hinder the future of the anti-opium policy. Therefore, two implementation measures for the prohibition of narcotics and opium have been re-promulgated, adding to the various effective regulations that have already been issued, and strengthening cooperation with all sectors of society to jointly combat drugs and opium. For highly addictive drugs, it is stipulated that there will be a two-year deadline from the year 24 to the end of the year 25 to completely eliminate them. In the first year, severe criminal penalties will be imposed, and after the deadline, from the year 26 onwards, all offenders will be sentenced to death without leniency. As for the cunning criminals who manufacture and traffic drugs, they will be executed at any time. Even those who assist the criminals will be sentenced to fixed-term imprisonment according to the standards of each year, without any exceptions. The aim is to achieve the effect of eradicating evil within the shortest possible time. Regarding the prohibition of opium, a six-year deadline is set, from the year 24 to the end of the year 29. For the prohibition of cultivation, it is stipulated that each province must conduct a general inspection of opium seedlings once a year during the period when they emerge from the soil. At that time, the Commission will also send special commissioners to the provinces to supervise the inspections, to ensure that there is no resurgence in the inland provinces where cultivation is absolutely prohibited, and that the standards for annual reduction in cultivation are practical in the remote provinces. Regarding the trafficking, sale, and consumption of opium, in addition to strictly controlling and managing them in accordance with the existing anti-opium regulations, more detailed measures for mutual association and deduction, which are reduced annually, are also stipulated to ensure that there is no room for embellishment or pretext. At the same time, the performance of local officials in enforcing the prohibition of narcotics and opium will be evaluated as a basis for rewards and punishments. Furthermore, local self-governance and self-defense organizations, as well as Party, government, military, schools, factories, and other institutions, will be tasked with promoting the prohibition of narcotics and opium to awaken the public. From the Office of the Commander-in-Chief to the provinces, cities, and counties, fair and dedicated individuals will be recruited to form anti-opium committees at all levels to jointly assist in the prohibition of narcotics and the cessation of opium, to ensure that officials are cautious and society follows suit, to encourage each other and work together to achieve success. It must be understood that the prohibition of narcotics and opium is vital to the nation and the people, and is related to the rise and fall of our entire nation. No matter what difficulties or obstacles there may be, we must do our utmost to eradicate them in order to achieve the goal of a two-year prohibition of narcotics and a six-year prohibition of opium. If this method is followed, and all provinces work together, the entire nation will join forces, and there is no reason why it cannot be achieved. It is hoped that the governors and mayors of each province will understand this intention, lead their subordinates, and strictly follow the procedures stipulated in these two measures. If there are still those who outwardly comply but inwardly defy, or who are perfunctory and neglect their duties, they will be severely punished for the crime of dereliction of duty and harming the people, once the facts are verified through random inspections. In addition to reporting to the National Government for record-keeping and issuing separate orders, the two implementation measures for the prohibition of narcotics and opium are urgently sent to the provincial and municipal governments for compliance, and the progress of compliance should be reported at any time. This order is issued.

Measures for Opium Prohibition: Article 1. The procedures for opium prohibition shall be carried out in accordance with the Measures for Dispatching Personnel to Investigate and Prohibit Opium Cultivation promulgated by the Office of the Commander-in-Chief, the Regulations for Strictly Enforcing Opium Cessation and Eliminating Opium-Smoking Households, the Regulations for Strictly Prohibiting Opium Cultivation in Inland Provinces, the Regulations for Strictly Implementing the Production of Native Opium in Border Provinces, the Regulations for Strictly Prohibiting Narcotic Drugs, and other opium prohibition regulations. Article 2. The eight provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Fujian are all absolutely prohibited from cultivating opium. A general inspection will be carried out from April of this year, and commissioners will be selected or personnel will be designated to go to each province to work with the provincial government to earnestly supervise and urge the implementation. If opium seedlings are still found in the counties that have already reported their prohibition, once verified, the county magistrate, the investigation committee, and the district chiefs, village heads, and planting households will all be severely punished according to military law. If there are gatherings to resist the eradication, the military will be dispatched to strictly arrest the ringleaders and execute them immediately. If there are unscrupulous military police teams that protect the planting, and the county magistrate has difficulty stopping them, they may secretly report them for arrest and punishment. If the county magistrate does not report or eradicate the opium in the territory, or privately collects donations, they will be executed immediately once verified, to serve as a warning. In the future, an application for inspection shall be submitted and a guarantee shall be reported in accordance with the regulations each year during the planting season, and a general inspection shall be carried out during the emergence period to prevent any resurgence. Article 3. The provinces of Shaanxi and Gansu have been approved to prohibit planting in stages, and according to the reports of the two provinces, the prohibition will be completely eliminated in stages according to the original plan. The counties that have already reported their prohibition will be inspected in accordance with the previous article. The counties in the second and third phases of the two provinces that plan to prohibit planting shall also be completely eliminated within the period. Article 4. Each province and city shall register opium addicts in accordance with the Regulations for Strictly Enforcing Opium Cessation and Eliminating Opium-Smoking Households, and shall be completely registered within three months, and shall be enforced. A license for poor opium-smoking households shall be separately established, and simple measures shall be stipulated to eliminate registration obstacles, in order to obtain accurate opium addict statistics, which shall be the standard for annual reduction. No more registrations will be accepted after the deadline. If there are any omissions after the deadline, they shall all be detained and ordered to quit opium. The total number of people registered at the final registration deadline in the year 24 shall be the total number, and opium addicts shall be forced to quit opium in order of age, in five phases, with one year as one phase, and one-fifth shall be reduced each year as the minimum. In the first phase, by the end of the year 25, one-fifth of the opium addicts shall be reduced. In the second phase, by the end of the year 26, one-fifth of the opium addicts shall be reduced. In the third phase, by the end of the year 27, one-third of the opium addicts shall be reduced. In the fourth phase, by the end of the year 28, one-fifth of the opium addicts shall be reduced. In the fifth phase, by the end of the year 29, all opium addicts shall be completely eliminated. If the aforementioned opium addict registration measures in each province and city are not in line with the actual situation in each city, causing opium addicts to hesitate and dare not come forward to register, the provinces and cities may carefully review and formulate detailed implementation rules and submit them for approval and modification. Article 5. Party, government, military service personnel, and school staff and students shall be absolutely prohibited from smoking opium. Those who have already become addicted shall be allowed to report and quit within a limited time. Those who do not report or relapse after reporting shall be punished with the death penalty in accordance with military law. In addition to revising the Measures for Limiting the Opium Cessation Period for Party, Government, and Military Service Personnel and Students promulgated by the General Headquarters of the Henan, Anhui, and Hubei Provinces in September of the year 21, and promulgating and implementing the Regulations for Opium Cessation and Rehabilitation, the heads of Party, government, military, and school institutions, and leaders at all levels, shall be responsible for supervising and organizing rehabilitation. Article 6. Due to the limited opium cessation period in each province and city, before the year 29 of the Republic of China, the opium required by all opium-smoking households shall be purchased by specially permitted merchants in accordance with the quantity of statistics. They shall obtain a special procurement license in accordance with the Regulations for Strictly Implementing the Production of Native Opium in Border Provinces, go to the border provinces to purchase it, designate the transportation route, and temporarily follow the joint transportation procedures. The Opium Prohibition Supervision Office shall implement public transportation, and all opium shall be unloaded into public warehouses and distributed locally after reaching the destination. The standard for procurement and public transportation shall be the quantity required by opium-smoking households registered in the year 24, and the quantity required by opium-smoking households shall be verified and reduced year by year from the year 25. Private transportation shall be prohibited, and violators shall be treated as smugglers. Article 7. The Opium Prohibition Supervision Office shall, within two months after the completion of the supplementary registration of opium addicts in each province and city, determine the number of opium paste shops to be established in each province and city with the provincial and municipal governments, and submit the list together with the number of opium paste shops established in each province and city approved by the Opium Prohibition Supervision Office, as the final standard for the number of opium paste shops. The Regulations for Strictly Implementing the Establishment of Opium Paste Shops shall be strictly enforced, and the purchase and sale of opium paste shall be carried out in accordance with the regulations. The quantity of opium paste to be purchased shall be reduced year by year based on the quantity of goods required in the year 24, and the number of shops shall also be reduced year by year. Article 8. The Opium Prohibition Supervision Office shall be responsible for the elimination and sale of opium, and the Department of Civil Affairs of each province, the Public Security Bureau of each city, the county magistrate, or the Opium Prohibition Committee shall be the responsible authorities for the prohibition of opium cultivation and consumption, and the suppression of smuggling within their jurisdictions. However, if the Opium Prohibition Supervision Office has specially established anti-smuggling agencies or patrol teams within its jurisdiction, the agencies or teams shall be responsible for performing their duties in accordance with the anti-smuggling regulations, and the local authorities shall assist them at any time. Article 9. Each province, city, and county shall set up an opium prohibition committee within one month, and each association shall be responsible for assisting in the prohibition of opium cultivation and the cessation of opium. (1) A general opium prohibition committee shall be set up in the seat of the Office of the Commander-in-Chief, and fair and enthusiastic opium prohibition advocates shall be appointed as members. (2) An opium prohibition committee shall be set up in each city, and the general association may send personnel to participate when necessary. (3) An opium prohibition branch shall be set up in each county. Article 10. The expenses of the opium prohibition committee, the opium prohibition branch, the detoxification center, and the opium cessation center set up in each province, city, and county, as well as the subsidies for hospitals designated to handle detoxification and opium cessation, shall be funded by the following: (1) The license fees for opium-smoking households and opium paste shops that should be allocated in this locality. (2) Opium prohibition fines and the proceeds from the sale of the property of drug offenders confiscated and confiscated. (3) Subsidies levied by the Opium Prohibition Supervision Office from the quota of native opium sold in each province and city. (4) Special subsidies from the treasuries of each province and city. Article 11. The performance of local officials in handling opium prohibition matters shall be specially evaluated. The governors and mayors of each province shall be responsible for evaluating them once every three months, adding their comments, and reporting them to the Office of the Commander-in-Chief for verification on time, in order to implement rewards and punishments based on the merits of opium prohibition. The evaluation regulations and reward and punishment measures shall be formulated separately. Article 12. The opium-producing provinces of Sichuan, Yunnan, Guizhou, Chahar, Suiyuan, and Ningxia shall refer to the successful case of staged opium prohibition in Shaanxi and Gansu, and thoroughly investigate the number of counties, mu, and output of opium production in each province within the year 24, as the standard for the final output, and formulate a plan for annual reduction and report it to the Office of the Commander-in-Chief for approval. From the year 25, they shall be reduced and eliminated year by year at the same time. The provinces of Hebei, Shandong, and Shanxi shall also be inspected by special commissioners dispatched by the Office of the Commander-in-Chief, as in the inland provinces. Article 13. These measures shall be posted publicly by the military and political organs of each region within five days after the promulgation document is received, and all subordinates shall be notified.

Measures for Drug Prohibition: Article 1. The procedures for drug prohibition shall be carried out in accordance with the Provisional Regulations for Strictly Prohibiting Highly Addictive Drugs, and all shall be carried out in accordance with these measures. Article 2. If there are a large number of people using highly addictive drugs or privately injecting morphine in each province, city, and county, a detoxification center shall be set up immediately. From April of this year, the governments of each province, city, and county shall be responsible for raising funds to complete the establishment within three months, or expand and merge with the already established opium cessation center. However, in places where the number of drug addicts is not large, a hospital with excellent conditions may be designated to provide detoxification services. Article 3. The governments of each province, city, and county shall conduct on-site investigations at any time on whether the organization, equipment, rehabilitation procedures, and treatment methods of the detoxification center or the designated detoxification hospital established in each province, city, and county are appropriate, and whether the number of people admitted for rehabilitation has increased or decreased, and shall report them to the Office of the Commander-in-Chief for review on a monthly basis. The Office of the Commander-in-Chief shall, based on the reports, select personnel with rich medical experience to go to various places to inspect and correct any shortcomings. Article 4. Anyone who manufactures, transports, or sells drugs shall be sentenced to death in accordance with the regulations. Those who assist in the crime shall be sentenced to fixed-term imprisonment of not less than five years and not more than eleven years, depending on the severity of the circumstances. However, civil servants who assist in the manufacture, transportation, or sale of drugs shall be sentenced to death. Article 5. The houses supplied for drug production shall be confiscated. If they are rented, the landlord shall be confiscated and confiscated if they fail to report the situation, and the landlord shall be punished in the same way as an accomplice. From the year 26, anyone found to be manufacturing, transporting, or selling drugs, whether the principal or accomplice, shall be sentenced to death. Article 6. The private property of anyone who manufactures, transports, or sells drugs shall be confiscated and confiscated. All informants and handlers shall be given a bonus of 10% to 40% of the confiscated property, depending on the circumstances. Article 7. Those who use highly addictive drugs or inject morphine shall automatically report to the institute and quit within the year 24. If they are found to be using drugs privately without reporting, they shall be detained and sent to a detoxification center for rehabilitation. In the year 24, if there are still those who have not reported and are using drugs privately, in addition to being detained and sent to a detoxification center for rehabilitation in accordance with the preceding paragraph, they shall also be sentenced to fixed-term imprisonment of not less than five years. From the year 26, anyone who uses drugs or injects morphine privately shall be sentenced to death or life imprisonment. Article 8. Those who relapse after drug rehabilitation shall be sentenced to death in accordance with the regulations. However, those who automatically report for rehabilitation and relapse may be given a fixed-term imprisonment of not less than five years within the year 24. Article 9. Party, government, military, and school personnel who use highly addictive drugs or inject morphine shall be given a limited time to automatically report to the institute for rehabilitation, and those who violate shall be sentenced to death. Article 10. These measures, together with the Provisional Regulations for Strictly Prohibiting Highly Addictive Drugs promulgated by the Nanchang Office of the Commander-in-Chief on May 11 of the year 23, shall be posted publicly by the military and political organs of each region within five days after the promulgation document is received, and all subordinates shall be notified. They shall also be summarized into simple explanations and preached separately using the following methods, and earnestly persuaded. 1. Party, government, and military organs and schools and factories shall be organized by their responsible personnel to convene their respective staff, soldiers, students, or workers on a regular basis. 2. Each city and county shall be responsible for the police and local self-government Lian Yuan by the Public Security Bureau, Wei District Chief, and convene residents in their respective jurisdictions on a regular basis. 3. Every three months, each province, city, and county shall jointly hold a large-scale anti-drug propaganda meeting with two Party, government, military, and school groups and other legal organizations, and may be supplemented by recreational performances or costume parades to promote social attention. Article 11. A general anti-drug inspection shall be carried out once a year from the year 24. The Chief of the Military Affairs Commission and the Office of the Commander-in-Chief shall send personnel to conduct open and secret visits to various places to inspect the results of drug prohibition in each province, city, and county, and severely punish them. Article 12. These measures shall be implemented ten days (five days) after the promulgation document is received.

Anhui Province Work Relief Begins—Dredging Rivers and Building Roads Simultaneously 97

Wuhu Correspondence: The two projects of dredging lakes and rivers and building roads in Anhui Province have begun to be implemented at the end of last month. In addition to the project funds that have been allocated by the Department of Finance, the relief grain has been distributed by Wuhu Grain a few days ago in accordance with the number, so various urgent projects are being actively carried out. Now, Pei Yixiang, Director of the Provincial Water Conservancy Project Office, has been awarded the regulations of Article 3 of the Work Relief Method, and the work relief is calculated according to the cubic foot, and 2 liters of grain are given for each cubic foot. However, the amount of relief grain is limited, and those who need both grain and silver will be combined with 1 dime of silver and 1 liter of grain for calculation. There are regulations for the price of ordinary cubic feet, either grain or silver. However, the construction sections are different, and the geological conditions are different. In the event of difficult work such as high banks on both sides, which takes time to send soil, and hard soil, which is difficult to excavate, the amount of soil that can be made in one day will inevitably be greatly reduced. If the price is still given according to the original regulations, it is not a fair way. Also, in ordinary places, the square price earned by each worker each day is only enough to feed themselves, and even if there is a surplus, it is not much. If there is no other remedy in case of continuous heavy rain that prevents work, there is bound to be a shortage of food. In view of the circumstances, two copies of the measures for adding grain to remote and difficult soil and for giving grain for rainy days when work is stopped have been prepared and sent to the Construction Department for review and filing. Director Liu Yiyan of the Department of Construction said that the proposed measures for adding grain to remote and difficult soil and for giving grain for rainy days when work is stopped are intended to consider the facts and supplement the original work relief method, and the review is still feasible. He specially signed a request to the Provincial Government for review and filing, which has been submitted to yesterday's standing meeting for resolution and approval. The two measures are recorded as follows: (Measures for Adding Relief Grain to Remote and Difficult Soil) 1. For those whose soil is far away more than 60 meters away, 5 liters to 1 liter of relief grain will be added for each cubic foot. 2. For those whose soil height is above 6 meters, 5 liters to 1 liter of relief grain will be added for each cubic foot. 3. For those whose soil is exceptionally hard and difficult to excavate, 5 liters to 1 liter of relief grain will be added for each cubic foot. 4. The above grain addition methods will be determined separately by the project offices within the limit according to the circumstances. (Measures for Giving Rations on Rainy Days When Work is Stopped) 1. If there is light rain during the work period, work shall not be stopped under any pretext. 2. If the work is completely stopped due to heavy rain for no more than two consecutive days, no additional grain will be given. 3. If the work is completely stopped due to heavy rain for more than two consecutive days, 1 liter of grain will be issued to each person per day from the third day. 4. If the number of days of work stoppage due to heavy rain is too long even if it is not continuous, the project offices will handle it according to the circumstances. (5th)

Current Situation of Huangshan Construction—Completing Transportation, Organizing Scenic Spots—Planning and Implementing in Stages 98

Wuhu Correspondence: Huangshan, the famous scenic spot in Southeastern China, has been opened up with the help of contemporary celebrities invited by the Anhui Provincial Government Construction Committee after the Wuhu-Tunxi and Huizhou-Hangzhou roads were opened. The Construction Department specially sent Secretary Xu Chuanyou and Technician Jin Youpeng to the mountain to supervise the work. It has been on a scale for a year, so-called preliminary construction is also. However, during the period when the Jiangxi bandits fled to Southern Anhui, the buildings that dotted the scenic spots on the mountain were slightly damaged. Now that the bandits have been pacified, they have been gradually restored, and the scattered bandits in the vicinity have also been cleaned up by the garrison troops, and the Huangshan area is as peaceful as ever. Therefore, Xu Shiying, the standing committee member of the Huangshan Construction Committee, went to the mountain to inspect the construction project. In the past two weeks, Zhang Zhizhong, the director of education of the Central Military Academy, Yao Wencai of Nanjing Anhui Middle School, Professors Wang Caibai, Zong Baihua, Zhang Shiqijia of Central University, Wang Songnian, the principal of Wuhu Guanzhong Middle School, and dozens of male and female students of the Department of Art of Central University have successively passed through Wuhu to Huangshan for sightseeing, which proves that the mountain is extremely safe. Xu Chuanyou and Jin Youpeng, the commissioners stationed in the mountain for supervision and construction, said that since Pu Bei entered the mountain in the middle of last month, the mountain peaches were in full bloom, and the orchids were fragrant, with both color and fragrance, which made people intoxicated. It is no different from a fairyland on earth, and the small birds are constantly playing music, which is even more moving and nostalgic. After a few days, the weather suddenly turned cold, and the spring snow suddenly fell. The Lion Forest cloud sea suddenly presented a vast and spectacular view. At that time, Cheng Guanlin, a staff member of the mountain, happened to be in the Lion Forest and wrote an article "Watching the Cloud Sea in the Snow" to record the different scenery. As for the construction plan of the mountain and the implementation plan for this year, Xu Jin will separately plan and implement them according to the economic urgency and the actual needs. (1) Transportation construction, 1. Repair the telephone, 2. Complete the road from Xiaoyao Pavilion to Xiaobu Bridge, 3. Open up the route surrounding the Taoyuan residential area, 4. Create the road along the stream of Ziyunji, 5. Select and repair the important embankment of Taoyuan Village and Ziyunji, (3) Survey and use land, 1. Survey and draw blueprints for each household that has paid rent, 2. Survey and draw a general map of Ziyunji, 3. Survey and draw a detailed map of the boundaries of each district, (3) Organize scenic spots, Taohua Peak is named for the peaches produced. In recent years, many mountain peaches have been killed by woodcutters. Xu Shiying has ordered them to be replanted in time, and ordered a plum forest to be built at the foot of Qingtan Peak, which is a grand view in the spring and autumn seasons. (4) Public buildings, 1. Repair the destroyed buildings, 2. Complete the unfinished projects of preliminary construction, 3. Construction Committee office buildings, 4. Raise funds to build barracks and bunkers, 5. Create parks and sports fields as a standard for construction. As for the expenses required, the Anhui Provincial Government will allocate them in stages so that the famous scenic spots in the Southeast can be completed as soon as possible. (5th)

Wuxi—A Major Fire in Lihua Village Yesterday Morning 101

Lihua Village outside the North Gate of our county has always been a gathering place for grass houses in Jiangbei. On the 5th of this month, the Peng family of Shi Damazi in that place was set on fire once. Fortunately, it was extinguished and did not cause a major disaster. Suddenly at about 4:00 am yesterday (7th), the house caught fire again. Because it was late at night, it was not noticed beforehand. Before long, the raging flames soared, and the fire illuminated the sky, turning into a prairie fire, and spreading to nearby grass houses and tile houses. Although the fire brigades of each section tried their best to extinguish the fire, the fire was so fierce and it was difficult to get water in that place, resulting in the burning of more than four or five hundred houses, a total of 149 families, suffering heavy losses.

Department Approval for Delaying the Land Tax on New Buildings in Jiangsu Province 102

Recently, the Jiangsu Provincial Government newly established regulations for land tax on buildings, levying taxes on residential properties and increasing the tax rates. These regulations were approved by the Provincial Government meeting and scheduled for implementation. Upon hearing this news, business associations in various areas including this county and Suzhou immediately sent telegrams to various central ministries and departments, as well as provincial officials, requesting a suspension of the implementation. Yesterday, the county business association of this county received a response from the Ministry of Interior, stating that it had been approved by the Ministry of Finance to consult with the Jiangsu Provincial Government to temporarily postpone the new regulations for land tax on buildings. After receiving the approval, the association immediately sent telegrams to the Jiangsu Provincial Tax Supervision Committee, the Provincial Federation of Commerce, and the county government of this county for their information.

Request for Impartial Handling of the Rice Crisis in Changshu 103

Due to the actions of Commissioner Liu of the Office and the Director of the Business Tax Bureau, who ordered the closure of the Taifeng Rice Company while inspecting their accounts, rice merchants in Changshu went on strike. Despite the best efforts of Party and government agencies to mediate, no resolution was reached, and the crisis escalated, becoming difficult to manage. The Grain and Miscellaneous Beans Association of this county yesterday sent a special telegram to the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Department of Finance, pleading for their compassion and urging them to handle the Changshu rice case impartially and swiftly, so that the dispute could be resolved. They also requested that the Tax Bureau be instructed to conduct collections peacefully, benefiting both officials and merchants, and protecting the livelihoods of ordinary people, an act of kindness as great as mountains, and so on.

Arrest of Bandits by the Huangli Police Station in Changzhou 104

Xu Chengrong, a patrol officer of the Second Sub-Station directly under the Public Security Bureau of Huangli Town in Wujin County, recently received a confidential report that Yu XX and Chen Jiangbao, the perpetrators of the robbery and assault on Jiang Changshou's home in Nanzhuang Village, Second District of this county, in February of this year, were hiding in Danyang County. He immediately secretly ordered a senior policeman to take a line of informants to the address and capture them. They successfully apprehended the two bandits, Yu and Chen, and after a preliminary interrogation at the station, they were sent to the County Public Security Bureau on the 6th for transfer to the County Government for trial.

The Supervisory Committee of the Provincial Party Committee, during its thirty-third meeting on the 6th, discussed the disaster situation in Yixing, Liyang, Jintan, Danyang, Jurong, Lishui, Gaochun, Jiangpu, and Luhe counties for a long time. They unanimously agreed that the disaster situation in these counties was extremely severe, with people selling their children and with livelihoods completely cut off, a truly unbearable sight. They should telegraph the executive committee at the same level to consult with the Provincial Government and immediately find ways to provide relief and organize spring assistance to preserve the lives of the people.

Highway Administration Subsidizes Road Maintenance Fees 108

The proposal by the Highway Administration Office of the Construction Department to subsidize road maintenance fees for long-distance buses passing through various city roads has been approved by the Construction Department. Ten percent of the total operating revenue from buses passing through these city roads will be allocated as subsidies. If any road damage occurs, the relevant agencies can be notified at any time for repairs.

Yangzhou: Large Number of Clerks Dismissed 109

Magistrate Ma, due to the frequent late arrivals and early departures of clerks in the One-Two-Three Counters and the Reed Tax Office, specially installed attendance books at each counter to ensure timely arrival and work. Recently, during a roll call, Chief Clerk Huang Jianyi, Assistant Clerk Zhao Changling, and Grain Clerk Lou Yaozhang were all more than ten minutes late to their counters, and each was given a major demerit. Furthermore, Clerks Zhu Shouzhi, Yin Guisen, Zhang Wei, Zhu Ziyun, Chen Zihe, Zhou Houqing, Zhu Xueqiao, Yang Ziqing, Cheng Yaozu, Wang Ze, Wang Zhaoqian, Niu Guirong, Jiang Defu, Zhao Changsheng, Zhang Shaoquan, Hu Renshan, Li Binghua, Chen Shuquan, and Wei Zongkuan, a total of nineteen individuals, were all dismissed for failing to attend the roll call as a warning to others. Furthermore, all chief clerks were instructed to promptly and thoroughly check and clarify the grain and money collected by the dismissed clerks of each counter. Hereafter, all staff from the chief clerk downwards must be ordered to arrive at their counters at the prescribed time each day, with no absences or proxy sign-ins allowed. If a temporary absence is necessary for official business, it should be reported to the Land Tax Office, otherwise it will be treated as neglecting official duties.

Nantong: Vigorously Advancing Salt Production in Various Fields in Huainan 110

The Huainan salt production area was formerly divided into six fields: Xinshan, Wuyu, Anliang, Caodian, Fengjue, and Yuzhong. As the sea receded eastward and sandbanks expanded, the salt production in each field decreased daily, producing only 120,000 shi per year, which is less than one-fifth of the production in Huaibei. The field verification office has dispatched commissioners to inspect and decided on an improvement plan to move the fields closer to the sea and abandon the old "grass boiling" method, adopting the Huaibei solar salt production method. All former closed fields will be released for cultivation.

Gaoyou: Lake West Drought Relief Association Organizes a Fundraising Team 111

The Department of Finance telegraphed Nantong Magistrate Jin to, together with Director Bao of the Business Tax Bureau, take over the Nantong Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Office, which will be jointly collected by the Tax Bureau from now on. The drought in Lake West of this county is severe. Magistrate Cao and others have formed the Lake West Drought Relief Association. The association's first standing committee meeting yesterday resolved to organize a fundraising team, with Dong Zhongxin, Wu Zhongying, Wang Yunzhi, Wang Gaichen, Xia Deyou, Liu Jiansan, Zhang Zhengbang, Sun Shijun, and thirteen others as members, to solicit donations from all sectors. They also submitted a request to the county government for subsidies for loaning capital and seeds. After investigating the existing farmers' loan capital of more than 3,000 yuan, it is proposed to allocate a loan capital of 3,000 yuan and 1,400+ shi of grain stored in the Food Management Office for loans and seeds, to relieve the urgent need for spring ploughing in the disaster-stricken area of Lake West. It is still ordered that each recipient provide proper guarantees and return the loans separately at the autumn harvest. A submission has already been made to the county for forwarding to the Civil Affairs and Construction Departments to expedite the allocation of relief funds.

Jiashan: General Headquarters Strictly Urges Compilation of Conscripts 112

The General Headquarters of the County Defense Corps, upon receiving orders to select the second training team for the 23rd year, was personally selected by County Magistrate Yang Zhanchun, who personally selected names from the roster. Those selected were all citizens of the intellectual class, preparing for three months of training to be appointed as Baojia chiefs and Defense Corps officers in the future. Therefore, all treatments are considered more favorable than the previous term. The food alone has been increased from 3.5 yuan to 5 yuan per person per month, and military uniforms and books are all free. However, the public misunderstood it as being conscripted into the army, and fled one after another, or feigned illness to avoid service. Therefore, although the quota was set at 170 people, as of yesterday, only 21 people had reported. The General Headquarters, considering that the deadline had passed and could not be extended any longer, specially dispatched personnel to the villages from yesterday onwards, limited to the shortest possible time, to gather at the General Headquarters, awaiting screening and team formation, and sending them to the province for training. If they continue to delay, they will be forced to carry out the order and seal up their houses.

Jiaxing: Labor Relief Starts in the First and Fourth Districts 113

The Jiaxing Relief Association, in order to carry out labor relief, after meeting with the First, Fourth, and Fifth Districts, decided to proceed step by step. It is now known that the First and Fourth Districts have completed their planning and have already begun work. The First District includes two locations: Yujiajing Port and Jinjiajing Port. The Fourth District includes three locations: Chejiaqiao Port, Beishiqiao Port, and Fenxiang Port. There are many disaster-stricken farmers who have been recruited. The standard of daily work is to be able to carry two cubic meters of earth, and each person is issued two sheng of relief rice per day.

Hangzhou: Fire in Taipingmen Main Street 114

A fire broke out at the Zhu family's home at No. 153 Taipingmen Main Street in Hangzhou City at 8:30 PM on the 5th. The fire brigade and various community volunteer firefighters rushed to put out the fire, which was finally extinguished at 9:00 PM. A total of eight houses were burned down, with losses of over 3,400 yuan. The cause of the fire has been detained by the bureau for investigation.

The White Society Chinese Painting Exhibition, organized by Zhu Wenyun, a professor at the Xinhua Art Academy in Shanghai, Zhang Shuqi, a professor at Central University, and Pan Tianshou, a professor at the West Lake Art Exhibition, opened yesterday on the fourth floor of the YMCA. Factory Apprentice Steals Money and Flees to Hangzhou 116

Wang Ji, a 16-year-old student at the Qingcheng Cotton Cloth Factory in Shanghai, has been working for many years and is well-trusted by the factory. Unexpectedly, when ordered to withdraw money from a money shop, he stole over 600 yuan and fled to Hangzhou, staying at the Quan'an Hotel at the city station. He was discovered by the detective team, who recovered over 400 yuan and handed him over to the court. He has now been sentenced to a fine of 100 yuan as a warning.

Shaoxing: Large Fire Under the Chang'an Suspension Bridge 117

A large fire broke out under the Chang'an Suspension Bridge outside Chang'an in Shaoxing on the afternoon of the 6th. On that day, the owner of the autumn hat shop and his entire family went to the countryside to sweep the tombs and closed the shop. Unexpectedly, a remnant fire accumulated and caused a major fire. One account states that the fire started at the Huhesheng Rice Cake Shop and spread to more than ten houses, including the Huixing Nursery Shop, the Yuanxing Duck Shop, and the Yuan XX Meat Shop, destroying over a hundred houses. During the rescue, two firefighters from the Public Security Bureau's fire brigade were swept into the fire pit by the water. Although they were rescued, they were severely injured.

Crackdown on Kidnapping Case, One Bandit Killed 118

Gu Guanrong, the owner of the Guyihe Rice Shop in the Xilukou of the Fifth District of Shaoxing, was kidnapped by bandits a month ago. His family reported the incident to the Chalukou Police Team, which, together with villagers, set out to track down the bandits. The case was cracked in a mountain the next day, and the hostage, Gu Guanrong, was rescued safely. The bandits were engaged in combat, and one bandit, Mao Songlin, was shot dead on the spot, and the bandit leader, Zhu Zulin, was captured alive. They were sent to the city on the afternoon of the 5th and transferred by the Public Security Bureau to the court for trial.

Haimen: Apprehension of Bandit Leaders 119

Zhang Jingtang, the captain of the Third District Detective Team of the Jiangsu Water Police, received a confidential report from an informant the day before yesterday that a large number of sea bandits were lurking in Lingdian Port, Haimen, intending to stir up trouble. Yesterday, he sent officers Chen Jianting and others to Haimen, together with the port police, to conduct a thorough search. The bandit leaders Wang Ruihua, Ma Defu, and Shen Sanmazi, as well as a bandit ship, firearms, and ammunition, were seized. According to the bandits, they had colluded in October of last year to rob the Qinglonggang Baofeng Wheelboat, the Xin'gang Cotton Boat, and ships carrying garlic and kerosene on the river. Chen and others escorted the bandits and the seized goods to the Baoshan Team Headquarters for interrogation.

Shanghai Preview of the London Art Exhibition Opens This Morning for Public Viewing, Displaying Over a Thousand Items from the Shang and Zhou Dynasties to the Song, Ming, and Qing Dynasties. Yesterday, Central Committee Members and Foreign Leaders Were Invited to Visit 121

The Shanghai preview of the London Exhibition of Chinese Art is now ready. Yesterday afternoon and morning, personnel from government agencies, Shanghai gentry, foreign guests, and related parties were invited to visit. The public exhibition will open today (the 8th) at 9:00 AM. Admission tickets are priced at two yuan per ticket and are sold at the Bank of China, the Shanghai Commercial and Savings Bank, the China National Products Company, and the China Travel Service Headquarters.

Exhibition Layout

The preview exhibition is located at the former site of the Bank of China on Shiji Road on the Bund. After the renovation by Huang Peijiang, the main entrance has been completely renewed. A banner with "Shanghai Preview of the London International Exhibition of Chinese Art" is hung over the entrance, with a flagpole and the national flag flying above it, making it extremely spectacular. Upon entering, there is a large lounge that can accommodate hundreds of people. Near the entrance is a guestbook for visitors to sign, and Chinese and English catalogs are available for sale. Around the room are displays of the Forbidden City Painting and Calligraphy Collection and the Forbidden City Weekly, which are available for sale during the exhibition. In addition, there is a cloakroom for guests to store clothing, hats, canes, and the like. Several kinds of flowers and trees are placed in the corners of the room, adding a lot of color. Exiting the room, follow the directional arrows to enter the first exhibition hall. On display here are paintings, calligraphy, folding fans, and embroidery from the Ming and Qing Dynasties. The second floor is divided into five exhibition halls. The second exhibition hall displays paintings and calligraphy from the Tang, Five Dynasties, Song, and Yuan Dynasties. The third hall displays bronzes. The fourth and fifth halls display porcelain from the Song, Jin, Yuan, Ming, and Qing Dynasties. The sixth hall displays rare ancient books, jade artifacts, selected archaeological examples, cloisonné enamel, carved red lacquer, agate, and rhinoceros horn. The Peking Library has twenty ancient books that have not yet been delivered, so the hall has several slanting bone glass cabinets to display them when they arrive. Overall, there are no fewer than nine hundred items on display, ranging from the Shang and Zhou Dynasties to the Ming and Qing Dynasties, all of which are precious and extremely magnificent.

Grand Occasion Yesterday

Yesterday (the 7th) at 8:00 AM, the exhibition hall opened its doors. Each member of the reception staff, wearing a blue gown and a black mandarin jacket with a reception badge, entered in an orderly manner and took up his position in each hall. The large lounge at the entrance and the small lounge inside were stocked with exquisite refreshments to welcome the guests. Key officials of the exhibition were also present to greet the guests. From 9:00 AM that day, the exhibition hall was busy with traffic and filled with Chinese and foreign guests. The exhibition presented each guest with a catalog for browsing. The grand occasion was unprecedented. In addition, dozens of people lingered outside the door without invitations, which shows the love of art in Shanghai.

Visiting Guests

Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, those who were invited to inspect the Central Party and government committee members and heads of various ministries and commissions were Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, Yu Youren, Dai Jitao, Kong Xiangxi, Cai Yuanpei, Wu Tiecheng, Yang Shukan, Liang Hancao, Chen Guofu (represented by Yao Dingchen), Wang Zhengting (represented by Liu Yunfang), Xue Dubi, Zeng Zhongming, Wang Luyi, Gui Chongji, Luo Jialun, Zhang Daofan, Zhu Peide, Chen Shuren, Zhou Qigang, Tang Shengzhi, Wang Shijie, Chuan Rulin, and Zou Lin. In addition, there were Pan Gongzhan, Wu Baofeng, Li Dijun, Sun Weilian, Shen Yi, Xiong Bin, Zheng Tianxi, and British Minister Sir Miles Lampson, and others, totaling over a hundred people. In the afternoon, foreign guests included Italian Ambassador Lojacono, Japanese Minister Akira Ariyoshi, Czech Minister Fierlinger, Swedish Chargé d'Affaires Linquist, Japanese Consul-General in Peking Suma Yakichiro, Commander of the Third Fleet Hyakutake, Military Attaché of the Japanese Legation Sato, and consuls from various countries stationed in Shanghai. Other guests included Wellington Koo and his wife, Wu Xingya, Cai Zengji, Wang Xiaolai, Yu Qiaqing, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Hu Bijang, Wu Yunzhai, Hu Puan, Wang Yishi, and members of the press, totaling no fewer than six hundred people. In the morning, the Minister of Education led the Education Department's director Lei Zhen and all reception staff to diligently greet the guests, presenting each person with a copy of the exhibition catalog.

Exhibition Arrangements

The exhibition hall is divided into two floors. The lower floor is for paintings and calligraphy, and part of the upper floor is also used for them. In front of each item, there is a wooden frame. To prevent the scroll from being too heavy, a silk ribbon is attached to the axis to secure it to the frame, avoiding damage. Books and albums are placed in glass display cases. Occupying most of the upper floor are bronzes, porcelain, jade artifacts, carved red lacquer, and other artifacts. Except for the scrolls, all items are displayed in glass cases. The display cases are sturdy and prevent fire. They can be disassembled, and there are small square seals on the screw joints, indicating strict security measures.

Overview of Paintings and Calligraphy

The reporter visited the preview twice yesterday, in the morning and afternoon. On the lower floor, the paintings and calligraphy of the Ming and Qing Dynasties were displayed, each with its own style in terms of brushwork and coloring. Among them, Shen Zhou's "Lu You Gao Tu," Chen Xianzhang's "Wan Yu Tu," Lu Ji's "Apricot Blossom and Peacock," Tang Yin's "Mountain Road Pine Sound," Qiu Ying's "Autumn River Waiting Ferry," Cui Zizhong's "Yin Bogu Tu," Guo Dian's "Crows and Geese at Dusk," Wang Hui's "Jiangcun Qingxia Tu" and "Yi Wu Xuan Tu," Yun Shouping's "Qiao Ke Xiu Zhu Tu," and Xue Tingxi's "Four Auspicious Celebrations," were particularly captivating, and visitors lingered, reluctant to leave. In the last room, glass cabinets displayed twenty folding fans, all the work of famous Ming and Qing artists such as Tang Yin, Qiu Ying, Wen Zhengming, and Dong Qichang. Ascending the stairs, the paintings and calligraphy from the Tang, Song, and Yuan Dynasties were displayed. First was Tang Xiaoli General (Zhaodao)'s "Luoyang Pavilion Diagram" and "Spring Outing Travel Diagram," as well as the works of an anonymous artist from the Five Dynasties. Preserved perfectly after a thousand years, they were truly rare sights. Next were the paintings and calligraphy of the Song Dynasty, such as Guo Xi's "Guan Shan Chun Xue," landscape paintings in color, Zhuang Gao Yi, Huizong's "Red Reed and White Goose," Li Di's "Returning Herdsman in Wind and Rain," Yan Cipings "Four Pleasures," an anonymous artist's "Moon Gazing in Empty Mountains," landscapes on cloth, Du Fu's "Beautiful Woman's Walk," and "Ruixue on Shanglin," and anonymous works. Yuan Dynasty works included Ni Yunlin's "Jiang'an Looking at Mountains" and an anonymous "Jiangtian Pavilion Tower". All of these works inspired countless sighs. In the glass cases were displayed the ink treasures and hand scrolls of famous figures from the Song, Yuan, and Ming Dynasties, such as the letters of the four great calligraphers Su, Huang, Mi, and Cai, Zhu Xi's letters, the hand scrolls of Zhao Mengfu and Huang Gongwang, and Xia Gui's "Ten Thousand Miles of the Yangtze River" scroll, which was over 33 feet long, a magnificent work depicting the entire Yangtze River from upstream to downstream. It was a pity that only a portion of it was displayed.

Song and Qing Embroidered Textiles

Next to the painting and calligraphy rooms, twenty-nine pieces of woven and embroidered silk from the Song and Qing Dynasties were displayed. Examples included Song Dynasty woven silk with water, flowers, and birds, especially white eagles, and Qing Dynasty woven silk depicting "Yu the Great Taming the Flood," "Zhou Chu Killing the Mosquitoes," "King Wu Receiving the Red Decree," and "Village Farmers Celebrating the Harvest." The exquisite weaving and embroidery were no different from paintings. Each scroll was imprinted with the Qianlong Imperial Treasure or added with an imperial postscript, making them extremely precious.

Bronzes, Porcelain, and Jade Artifacts

Next were the bronzes, classified and named with great precision, all from the Shang and Zhou Dynasties. The "Taotie Wen Lei," "Fang Lei Bu," "Zeng Bo Xi Hu," and "XX Gong Fang Zun" were all intricately carved. Their production dates were all over a thousand years before the Western calendar, five hundred years earlier than the Greek era, and a thousand years earlier than the Roman unification of Italy, proving that the culture and civilization of our country at that time were far ahead of Europe and the West. The bronzes from the Chu Kingdom unearthed in Shouxian, Anhui Province, were particularly rare and precious. Next were the porcelain pieces, all produced by famous kilns of the Song, Yuan, Ming, and Qing Dynasties. There were many types, and the craftsmanship was exquisite, unmatched by modern times. Next were the cloisonné enamel and the jade artifacts. Among them, the yellow jade linked ring seal with three seals and a chain were all carved from a single piece of jade, making the workmanship quite difficult.

Ancient Books and Oracle Bones

Finally, there were oracle bones, oracle bone weapons, and bronze weapons from the Academia Sinica, arranged in order, providing insight into the history of early human evolution. Next to them were rare ancient books, including Southern Song carved editions and Jin XXX editions, the earliest printed books in the world, as Europeans only began to manufacture paper in 1276, more than a hundred years after printing in our country. Next to the cabinets was an empty cabinet reserved for the rare books selected by the Peking Library. These ancient books would arrive and be displayed in the coming days.

Opening Today

The preview exhibition will officially open this morning. There will be no ceremony, and the public will be able to visit. In response to requests from all parties, the preparatory committee decided to add items used by Emperor Gaozong of the Qing Dynasty to the display to satisfy the visitors' wishes. The exhibition will also assign reception staff to each hall to take care of everything.

A Brief List of Exhibits

The general catalog printed by the preparatory committee provides detailed explanations of the history and region of the exhibits, and also notes their dimensions and weight. (1) Bronzes, further divided into cooking utensils and tableware, containers, warming utensils and drinking vessels, ordinary utensils, and musical instruments. Bronzes unearthed in Xinzheng and Shouxian are listed separately in two columns. The tableware category includes lei, li, ding, gui, ju, dou, and three-eight pieces. Except for the lian and deng, which are Han Dynasty items, the rest are all Shang and Zhou Dynasty items. The porcelain category includes sixty-four pieces from the Song Dynasty Ding ware, Jun ware, Ru ware, Guan ware, and Longquan ware. There are seventy-three pieces from the Ming Chuzhou, Shen Dehua ware, Yongle ware, and so on. President Wang Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning, Visited the Art Exhibition with Zeng Zhongming and Others at Noon, Hosted a Reception for Leaders from Various Circles in Shanghai, and Returned to Nanjing by Night Train Last Night 122

A dispatch from the Central News Agency reports that Wang Jingwei, President of the Executive Yuan, left Nanjing by night train at 11 o'clock the night before last and arrived at Zhenru at 7:10 yesterday morning. He went directly to his private residence on Bubbling Well Road to rest. President Wang's visit was to preside over the Shanghai preview of the London International Exhibition of Chinese Art and to host a reception for leaders from various circles in Shanghai. He returned to Nanjing by night train that evening. The details are recorded as follows:

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning, Returned to Nanjing Last Night

President Wang, along with Zeng Zhongming, took a night train from Nanjing to Shanghai at 11 o'clock the night before last. He arrived at Zhenru Station at 7:10 yesterday morning. Those who came to welcome him included Yang Hu, Director of the Shanghai Security Bureau, and Wang Zhinan, Secretary, and many others. The Zhenru Station and the Zhongshan Road area were guarded by security teams and police squadrons, and security was very tight. In addition to Zeng Zhongming, Ma Chaojun and Zhu Peide also accompanied him. After President Wang arrived at his private residence on Bubbling Well Road yesterday morning, he went to Dr. Noel's clinic at around 8 o'clock to have a physical examination and treat his old illness. More Than Four Million British Silver Dollars Arrived Yesterday by British Ship, Loaded on the Lunxi Ship Docked at the Gonghexiang Wharf, and Will Be Unloaded and Stored in the Vaults of the Three Banks Starting This Morning 123

The Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee, in order to stabilize the market, planned to purchase 20 million silver dollars and transport them to Shanghai to regulate the financial market. It entrusted the Hong Kong branches of the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications to handle the matter. It successively purchased about 3 million Hong Kong silver dollars. Later, due to the shortage of cash in Hong Kong, it changed to purchasing from London, England. The first batch of 3 million silver dollars has arrived in Shanghai. The second batch, loaded on the British Steamship Company's Lunxi, arrived yesterday morning and docked at the Gonghexiang Wharf on Broadway Road. Yesterday was Sunday, and the customs office was closed as usual. It was decided that starting today, employees of the Central Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Bank of Communications would be dispatched to unload and store the silver dollars in the vaults of the three banks. As for the total amount, a reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency met with a committee member of the committee last night, who said that it was more than 4 million silver dollars. As for the saying that another 1 million silver dollars would arrive tomorrow, he had not heard of it.

New Life Youth Service Corps Embarked on Work Yesterday, Serving Tirelessly in the Drizzle 124

Yesterday was a regular holiday. The New Life Youth Service Corps organized by the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association set out to serve again. The main points of their work were to rectify the traffic order in the city. It was reported that each group of the service corps that set out to work had more than 1,000 members. The association sent people to various districts to supervise the work of the members. The members worked very hard. Yesterday afternoon, despite the drizzle, they continued to work tirelessly. A reporter from the National News Agency went to the Datong Road area in Zhabei and Pudong and other places. The members of each group would step forward and kindly persuade pedestrians who did not comply with the rules of the road. Their attitude was kind and amiable, which moved the listeners. Therefore, the results were very good.

Japanese Consuls Meeting This Morning, Representatives from All Regions Arrived Yesterday, Ariyoshi Presides Over the Agenda Scheduled for Three Days 125

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, Ariyoshi Akira, the Japanese Minister to China, convened a meeting of consuls stationed in various parts of China in Shanghai, which was scheduled to be held at 10:00 this morning at the office of the Japanese Legation in Shanghai. The Japanese heads from various regions arrived in Shanghai one after another in the past two days. The proposals of each consul have been prepared, and the agenda has been prepared. The discussion will begin this morning, and then the results of the discussion will be reported by Ariyoshi. The details are recorded as follows:

Consuls Arrive in Shanghai

It is now known that the representatives from various regions attending the Japanese Consuls Conference in China, in addition to the Commercial Counselor of the Legation Yokotake and the Consul General in Nanjing Suma, who had arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday, the Japanese Consul in Hankou Miura, the Japanese Consul in Guangzhou Kawasoe, the Japanese Consul in Tianjin Kawagoe, the Japanese Consul in Jinan Nishida, the Japanese Consul in Qingdao Sakae, the Japanese Consul in Fuzhou Usami, and the Japanese Consul in Xiamen Tsukamoto, all arrived in Shanghai one after another yesterday by ship, train, or plane.

A Glimpse of the Proposals

According to personnel of the Japanese Legation, the proposals of each consul had been sent to Shanghai in advance and had been classified and included in the conference agenda by the legation. However, most of them were reports, such as the diplomatic, commercial, and political situation in the areas where each consul was stationed, as well as the issue of anti-Japanese goods, with attached opinions for the conference to study. At the meeting tomorrow, Japanese Minister Ariyoshi Akira will preside, and the secretaries of the legation will be responsible for the records. The meeting will be held from 10:00 to 12:00 in the morning and from 4:00 to 5:00 in the afternoon every day, and will be closed after three consecutive days.

Report by the Japanese Minister

According to the spokesperson of the Japanese Legation, Commercial Counselor Yokotake, after arriving in Shanghai yesterday afternoon, went to visit Minister Ariyoshi to report on the progress of the negotiations in Japan and to convey various news from the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs. There was no need for another meeting yesterday. As for Minister Ariyoshi's return to China, it was decided that he would leave on the 20th, accompanied by his wife and Secretary Kozawa. Before returning to China, Ariyoshi will of course have to go to Nanjing to bid farewell to the important officials of the central government and make the latest contact with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on various diplomatic issues between China and Japan.

Former Governor of the Philippines Arrived in Shanghai, Plans to Stay for Two Months Before Returning to the United States 126

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, Harrison, the former American Governor of the Philippines, recently arrived in Shanghai from Europe with his fourth wife. He arrived at the port on the Italian ship Conte Verde the day before yesterday afternoon. After arriving in Shanghai, Harrison was unwilling to express any opinions on the issue of Philippine independence. He only said that since he left the Philippines in 1921, he had never done any research on the politics of the island, so it was inconvenient for him to talk about it. Harrison was born in New York, USA in 1873, graduated from Yale University in 1895, participated in the Spanish-American War, served as a member of the US Congress from 1903 to 1913, and was promoted to Governor of the Philippines in the same year, until he resigned in 1921. This time he came from Scotland, England, and will stay in Shanghai for two months before returning to the United States.

Wang Zhiyuan Talks About the Current Situation of Overseas Chinese is Still Good 127

According to Hua Dong News Agency, Wang Zhiyuan, Secretary-General of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, came to Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday morning. A reporter from Hua Dong News Agency met him at the Shanghai preview of the London Art Exhibition and immediately asked him about the current situation of overseas Chinese. According to Wang, in the past, overseas Chinese were affected by the world market recession, so it was difficult to maintain their businesses, and they returned to China one after another. However, recently, the industry and commerce in the Nanyang Islands and other places will enter a period of recovery, and overseas Chinese can still gain a foothold, so the current situation is still good. Recently, overseas Chinese going abroad have been very enthusiastic. Wang also said that the Qiaole Village set up by the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission in Anhui has achieved good results, especially the returned overseas Chinese who can work hard to manage and develop the village. The village is currently limited to single overseas Chinese, and in the future, it is planned to allow overseas Chinese to live with their families and children.

Traces of Contemporary People 128

Zhu Peide, Chen Shaokuan, and Ju Zheng took the 11 o'clock night train to Nanjing last night.

Li Mingyu's Arrest Case, Lawyers Lou and Xu Write to Various Circles, The French Consul General Has Not Yet Responded, Which is a Deep Regret, Jin Xi's Old Hatred Has Not Ended, and Mr. Cui's New Creation Has Arrived Again, Hoping that Various Circles Will Urge the Authorities to Make Strong Protests 129

According to Xin Xin News Agency, lawyers Lou Yunmei and Xu Jie released a letter to various circles yesterday regarding the arrest of Cui Yingxin (aka Li Mingyu), a Korean naturalized in China. The original text is excerpted as follows:

Mr. Cui Quxin's Arrest Process

To all compatriots, please be aware that the existence of foreign concessions within our country is based on the exercise of the national administrative power and allows foreign residents to have the right to reside in groups. It does not mean that our country loses its sovereignty within the concessions. The establishment of the French Concession Police Department in Shanghai is based on the agreement on the establishment of a Chinese court in the Shanghai French Concession. According to Article 6 of the agreement, any criminal arrested in the concession, excluding holidays, should be sent to the competent court within 24 hours. If the court is not delivered after the deadline, the criminal should be released immediately. Furthermore, according to the first paragraph of Article 7, no criminal may be transferred to government offices outside the concession without first being interrogated by the competent court. However, the Shanghai French Concession Police Department suddenly arrested Cui Yingxin (aka Li Mingyu), a Korean naturalized in our country on June 13, 1925, at Xiechengli, Rue de la Mission in March 26 of this year. At that time, Cui presented his naturalization certificate to explain the misunderstanding and requested exemption from detention. However, the police department ignored it and confiscated the naturalization certificate.

The French Consul General's Office Has Not Yet Responded

Later, Cui's wife hired our lawyers to negotiate with them, but it was ineffective. We received a reply from Mr. Gable of the Police Department on April 4, stating that he had been handed over to the Japanese Consulate General in Shanghai on the same day. We then visited the French Consul General Baili Ong to reason with him. He claimed that he was completely unaware of the incident. Although he agreed to investigate and handle the matter according to law, more than ten days have passed and there has been no response. We cannot help but feel infinite regret. Since Cui has been naturalized in China, regardless of whether he is suspected of committing a crime, he should be bound by the above-mentioned agreement and handed over to the Shanghai Second Special District Local Court for trial. How can he be arrested and handed over arbitrarily? This kind of behavior not only endangers the safety of residents in the French Concession, but simply destroys our country's sovereignty. How can all our citizens silently accept it? It is found that the police department has arrested Koreans naturalized in our country more than once without any reason. Jin Xi's old hatred has not ended (Jin Xi was arrested by the French Consulate in Shanghai in October 1922 and transferred to the Japanese Consulate General in Shanghai), and Mr. Cui's new creation has arrived again. How can we bear such arbitrary destruction? And this time, Mr. Cui's arrest was unknown to the French Consul General's Office, so the strangeness of the situation is even more different from the past. Leaving aside the fact that France is also an advanced country of independent countries, whether legally or rationally, the French Police Department should not accept a letter of entrustment from the Japanese Consul General in Shanghai and hand over the criminal directly, willingly acting as an affiliated institution of another country and losing its status as a great power. Our country is not comparable to a country that has been subjugated and has completely lost its sovereignty. How can we despise it so much?

Urge the Authorities to Make Every Effort to Protest

We believe that the reason why Koreans have been happy to naturalize in our country in recent years is because they are unwilling to be humiliated by the subjugation of their country, and they share the same feelings for the revolution, hoping to move towards a bright field. Then, how should our country uphold Dr. Sun Yat-sen's instructions, unite with small and weak nations, and struggle together? Now, we cannot provide the minimum level of residence protection, and they are being destroyed by foreign countries in our country. If we were in their position, what attitude would people take towards our country? Our lawyers are speaking according to the law and are reluctant to make too many comments. Fortunately, there are still celebrities in the country who will definitely understand the interests of China and Korea. How should we urge the authorities to make strong protests against this unacceptable infringement? It is not too late to mend the fold after a sheep is lost. It is not possible to seek real benefits for Mr. Cui alone, and when the Sino-French agreement expires, it will not be difficult to use it as a basis for negotiation when advocating the recovery of police power. Our lawyers have more than enough heart but not enough strength, so we will list the details of the case to present it. We hope that all compatriots will not ignore it because it is Mr. Cui's personal matter.

There, a tea server named Li Abao fell in love with her and secretly hid her to live together. However, whether this is true or not cannot be determined yet. He requested that the case be postponed for further investigation and that the defendant be detained. However, she did see Busy Zi and Li Abao whispering to each other at the entrance of Kunshan Garden, but she did not know what they were saying. Her testimony was evasive. Judge Jiang Shuzi ordered her to be remanded in custody for further investigation and verification.

Woman Driving, Crushing a Monk to Death 137

Wei Tao Lan, a woman residing at No. 25, Lane 100, Henry Road in the French Concession, is twenty-two years old this year and a native of Nanjing, also known as Yangzhou. The day before yesterday afternoon, she was driving her own car, license plate number 11818, along Dada Road in the French Concession from east to west. When she reached the front of No. 409, west of the Dongzilaihuo Street intersection, an elderly man named Wang Huaiyu, about sixty years old, wearing monk robes, was crossing the road from south to north. Wei immediately braked, but the rear right fender of her car still collided with Wang, causing him to fall to the ground. A patrolman saw this, recorded the license plate number, helped Wang into Wei's car, and took him to the police station. The detective chief ordered him to be sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, Wang died at 3:30 AM the next morning due to his injuries. The hospital notified the police station, who sent detectives to transport the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Parlor for an autopsy. As no relatives of the deceased were found, the police station reported to the Second Special District Court, which appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren to come to the parlor with a forensic doctor and a clerk to examine the body. They then held a court hearing. First, the Western detective Kelaixi (transliteration) reported the investigation of the case. The official then questioned the defendant, Wei Tao Lan, and the witness, Wei Jiqing (thirty years old, from Yangzhou, the defendant's elder brother, working as a partner at a cigarette and paper shop at No. 90, Father Jin Road, who was also in the defendant's car at the time of the incident), about what happened. They ruled that Wang Huaiyu died from injuries sustained from being knocked down. The body was photographed and prepared for burial by the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Parlor. Whether the defendant was at fault would be investigated and dealt with by the police department. After the autopsy, the defendant, Wei Tao Lan, paid for a coffin and clothing, which were delivered to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Parlor for burial yesterday. The body will be transported to the cemetery pending family identification.

Father and Daughter Sue, Seeking Divorce from the Live-in Son-in-Law 139

Hou Xiang Sheng, a native of this county, is over fifty years old and lives in Houjiazhai, Jiangwan, earning a living by farming. His wife, Li, only gave birth to one daughter, Xi Nv, who is twenty-four years old and cherished. Because Hou Xiang Sheng was worried about having no son, he sought a good son-in-law to rely on in the future. The judge said that since the testimony was one-sided, it was difficult to believe. He said that family lawsuits were different from other civil lawsuits and required the defendant to appear in person to express his intentions. Since the defendant did not appear today, mediation was impossible. He ordered that a formal lawsuit could be filed five days later. After the ruling, the court adjourned.
