City Infectious Disease Hospital, New Building Officially Completed, Future Efforts to Expand and Improve, Further Construction of Kitchen and Wards Planned 141

The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, recognizing that various infectious diseases are prevalent in the city, sought to protect the health of its citizens. Therefore, it obtained approval from the Municipal Government several years ago to establish an infectious disease hospital at the original site of the Zhabei Public Hospital. However, the old buildings inside were not suitable for use, so a new building was rebuilt. It has now been officially completed. In the future, it is planned to expand and add seven wards to make it complete. The details are as follows:

New Building Completed

The Municipal Infectious Disease Hospital was established on the original site of the former Zhabei Public Hospital. It began admitting patients on March 10th of last year. However, the health bureau authorities believed that the original hospital buildings were not suitable for isolation and could not accommodate a large number of beds. The buildings on the east side of the hospital were destroyed during the Shanghai War and could not be repaired. Therefore, to facilitate treatment and management, it obtained approval from the Municipal Government to allocate 37,000 yuan to plan and build a new building in conjunction with the Public Works Bureau in the spring of last year. Construction began in early July, including the construction of two new-style wards, each capable of accommodating thirty-five beds. The internal facilities were all new-style and easy to isolate and disinfect. The project has now been fully completed and officially opened.

Plans for Expansion

According to Wu Liguo, the director of the hospital, although the new building has been rebuilt and officially established, it has not been possible to expand as much as desired due to limited funds, which is regrettable. It is planned to gradually develop as the city treasury becomes more abundant. Currently, the most urgent need for improvement is the kitchen. Whether the kitchen of an infectious disease hospital is clean or not is of great importance. The current kitchen of the hospital is quite simple. It is planned to raise funds in the near future and immediately build it. As for the wards, seven more wards need to be added so that the nine statutory infectious diseases can each have their own place for isolation. In other aspects, such as disinfection, because the existing disinfection room is too small, it is also planned to build another corner. In short, the hospital will expand as much as its economic power allows to make the interior more complete.

Minsheng Company's Minquan Ship Launched Yesterday, Ship's Equipment is Extremely Perfect 142

The Minquan ship, newly built by Minsheng Industrial Company, was launched for trial operation yesterday morning at 10:00 AM. It departed from the Qiuxin Factory on Jichang Street in the Nanshi District and traveled to Longhua, where it stopped on the river. The reporter also went on the ship. The Shanghai manager of the company, Mr. Zhang Shusen, gave a detailed account of the ship's situation. The details are as follows:

History of the Minquan

The ship was originally named Longmao and owned by the British Longmao Foreign Firm. In the 13th year of the Republic of China, it was sold by Jiangmao Foreign Firm to Taikoo Foreign Firm and renamed Wanliu. In the 22nd year of the Republic of China, after it was sold to the company, it began to be rebuilt, which took more than ten months to complete. It is 29 feet and 11 inches long, 31 feet wide, 10 feet deep, and has a draft of 8.4 feet. The speed is approximately 14 nautical miles per hour. The gross tonnage is 1191.76 tons, and the net tonnage is 686.17 tons.

Capacity of the Ship

The ship can carry more than 1,900 bales of cotton yarn and accommodate 164 passengers. Each person has a comfortable berth. The need for steerage berths is greatest on direct voyage ships. The largest passenger cabin on a ship traveling on the Sichuan River is the Mingui of this company, which can only carry 112 people. Now the Minquan ship can accommodate 50 more people, especially in the steerage berths.

Layout of the Cabins

The large deluxe cabins are located on the third floor. The front section has five rooms, each accommodating two people, with complete equipment and everything available. The official cabins are located at the rear of the third floor and have nine rooms, each accommodating two people (most of the official cabins on ships have upper and lower berths, but on the Minquan ship, each person occupies one berth) and each has a wardrobe. The room cabins are located on the second floor. The front section has seven rooms, each accommodating four people. The steerage cabins are located at the rear of the second floor and are divided into male and female cabins. The male steerage cabin can accommodate 92 people, and the female steerage cabin can accommodate 16 people (ships do not usually have female steerage cabins, which is inconvenient for single female passengers. This is unique to the Minquan ship).

Air Circulation

The light and ventilation in the ship's cabins of all classes are very complete. Not only do the large deluxe cabins have ventilation windows, but the steerage cabins also have a ventilation window, all leading directly to the top floor for air circulation, making it cool in summer. In addition, all classes of cabins and lounges have heating equipment.

Sanitary Equipment

The large deluxe cabins have one male and one female bathroom each, and two male and two female toilets each. The official cabins have one male and one female bathroom each, and two male and two female toilets each. The room cabins have one male and one female bathroom each, and one male and one female toilet each. The steerage cabins have one male and one female bathroom each, five male toilets, and two female toilets.

Luxurious Lounges

The ship's fourth-class cabins all have lounges, so that guests have a place to relax after meals. The ones in the large deluxe cabins and official cabins are even more magnificent, with carpets, table covers, chair covers, curtains, vases, etc., all being domestic products. The lights in each lounge are installed around the edges of the ceiling, so that the light is emitted from all around, not too strong, and more aesthetically pleasing, and can also avoid the gathering of small insects in summer and autumn.

Sand Filtered Drinking Water

Most ships use alum to clarify and precipitate passenger drinking water, which is already considered elaborate, but it cannot be thoroughly clarified. This ship uses extremely fine sand to filter the water, making the filtered water extremely clean, emphasizing hygiene.

Legitimate Pastimes

In addition to the above-mentioned features, the ship also has books, a radio receiver, a bulletin board, ordinary musical instruments, etc., for the entertainment of passengers.

Missing One Seal on a Transfer Slip, Attempting to Defraud One Thousand Yuan, Shen Heqing Suddenly Appeared, The Court Must Investigate the Case 144

There was business dealings between the Xie Feng Foreign Cloth Store at No. 2, Lane 249, Ningbo Road, and the Yongxing Money Shop at No. 11, Lane 120, Ningbo Road. If Xie Feng needed to draw cash from a check, it would instruct its apprentice to go to Yongxing to collect it with a transfer slip. However, the seals on the transfer slip for issuing checks and collecting cash were of two different styles. At 1:10 PM the day before yesterday, Xie Feng sent apprentice He Yaoliang with a transfer slip to Yongxing to collect a check paper worth 245 yuan with a ten-day term. However, when He was passing the intersection of Henan Road and Beijing Road, a man from Ningbo named Shen Heqing suddenly chased after him from behind and told He that he had just received instructions from the manager saying that he needed to collect another 1,000 yuan in cash. So, he took the transfer slip and filled out a receipt for 1,000 yuan in cash. He, unaware that it was a fraud, took the slip to Yongxing. After the shop examined the transfer slip, they suspected it because Xie Feng always had a different seal when collecting cash. So, they called Xie Feng, who told them that they had no request to collect 1,000 yuan in cash. Based on this, they questioned He, who told them everything. The shop then wrapped a package in paper, simulating a 1,000-yuan bill, and instructed He to return to the store along the same route, while sending someone to secretly follow him. However, when He was walking to the intersection of Henan Road, Shen Heqing indeed came forward again, intending to take the 1,000-yuan bill. He was then captured by the pursuers, patrolman Geng Debiao and Chinese constables No. 3358. Shen was arrested and taken to the general police station. Yesterday, he was taken to the First Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, explained the case and prosecuted him under Article 226, Section 1 of the Criminal Law. When questioned, Shen Heqing only claimed that he was temporarily confused. Judge Feng Shide reviewed the confession and ruled that the case still needed investigation and ordered his detention. The case will be heard again at a later date.

Jin Jiulin, Inspector General of the Special Agency of the French General Police Department, detectives Zhang Ziying, Zhou Bingcheng, and Bao Tan Cui Zhenguo, etc., arrested the famous kidnapping gang Geng Huatang (from Jinan, former adjutant of the Songhu Military Governor's Office), Zheng Tangsheng (local, former practitioner at the Gold Exchange), Shang Zhen (from Henan, former division commander), Liu Yimin (from Yangzhou, first a car driver, then a soldier), Wu Shaoting (from Yangzhou, former employee on the Taikoo Yangtze River liner), and more than ten others in Tianjin in July of the 22nd year of the Republic of China. The court, not being reluctant to seek details, transferred documents to Tianjin, Hangzhou, Yichang, Chuzhou, Putuoshan, and other organs, groups, and temples for investigation, and summoned the victims and witnesses presented by Zheng and others to the court for identification and cross-examination. The details have been previously reported. It is now learned that the retrial of this case began on November 8th of the 22nd year of the Republic of China and has lasted for one and a half years. The court has been held more than ten times. Although each defendant has overturned the original trial's confessions, the confessions made in each court session are also inconsistent and contradictory. At 10:00 AM the day before yesterday, Judge Wang held a court session for further trial. Fei Xizhen, a lawyer from the police department, appeared in court, and the defense lawyers hired by the defendants also arrived on time. The judge first ordered each defendant to be questioned one by one, and then summoned the abbot of the Baoben Hall of Putuoshan, Monk Xin Zheng, to court. After questioning Shang Zhen about his arrival and departure from the mountain, the court considered the investigation of evidence to be complete and ordered the debate to begin. After Fei, the lawyer from the police department, and the lawyers for each defendant debated in succession, the court declared the debate concluded and scheduled the sentencing for the 12th. Zheng was still remanded to the detention center to await instructions.

at the Guyi Garden

Tang Sanbian, Cohabits with the Wife of a Deceased Friend, Stopped Visiting After Giving Birth to a Daughter, Repeatedly Sued for Support 147

Tang Sanbian, a Cantonese residing at No. 117, Ronghua Lane, Xinjihang Road, is 44 years old and works at the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company factory, earning about one hundred yuan per month. Li Lin, a colleague of Tang's, died of illness in the 20th year of the Republic of China. Because Tang was a close friend of Li's, he often visited Li's home. Unexpectedly, he developed a relationship with Li's wife, Xie. He then rented a room at No. 45, Tongqing Lane, Broadway Road. On November 29th of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, she gave birth to a daughter named Ailian. Recently, Tang suddenly stopped visiting her. After she learned that Tang actually had another wife, she sued Tang for abandonment, etc., in the Criminal Division of the First Special District Court. As a result, she lost the case. Now, Xie has hired a lawyer to file another lawsuit for support in the Civil Division of the First Special District Court. Yesterday, Judge Peng Shi held a hearing in the Fourteenth Court. Tang Sanbian claimed to be ill and did not attend. His lawyer attended on his behalf. Xie stated the details of her relationship with Tang and claimed that she was currently suing the defendant for four reasons: (1) to confirm that she is a member of Tang Sanbian's family, (2) to confirm that Ailian was born to Tang Sanbian, (3) to order Tang to pay her 2,500 yuan for living expenses, and (4) to order him to pay her 3,400 yuan for Ailian's education expenses. She also presented four letters written by Tang in his own handwriting to prove the relationship between the plaintiff and Ailian and the defendant. Tang's lawyer denied that the defendant had a cohabitation relationship with the plaintiff. Judge Peng ruled that the case still needed to be summoned and rescheduled the hearing.

United Rice Merchants Association, Stipulates the Route for Rice Boats to Shanghai, Dredging Project of the Wusong River Estimated to Take Three Months 148

After the Taihu Lake Water Conservancy Commission breached the dam at Yujidun and dredged the river, rice boats must detour to Shanghai. Yesterday, the United Rice Merchants Association of North Shanghai announced four loading ports for rice boats to various places: (1) smaller boats can go from Zhaotun Bridge, Sijing, Qibao to Longhua Port, through South Huangpu to Wusong River; (2) go from the four ports to Qingpu, pass Songjiang, bypass Xijiaowan at Guanyeji and enter from Minhang; (3) transport from Zhujiajiao, Shizihe, Maota, Jiangzong Port, Tagang, Xijiaowan to Shanghai. As for the river dredging project, it is expected to take three months to complete.

The Rickshaw Pullers Request the City Government to Negotiate with the British Works Department to Cancel Rickshaw Registration and Recover the Mutual Aid Society; External Approval Requests City Government to Investigate and Verify 149

Xin Xin News reports: Regarding the case of the city's rickshaw pullers requesting the British Works Department to cancel rickshaw registration and recover the rickshaw pullers' mutual aid society, the issue remains unresolved. On the 6th, the association again sent representatives to petition the city government, requesting them to negotiate with the British Works Department. The details are recorded below:

Representatives Petition

Rickshaw puller representatives Chen Guoxie and others, seeking to negotiate with the British Works Department authorities to cancel rickshaw registration and recover the rickshaw pullers' mutual aid society, so that labor and management can handle it themselves, went to the city center district on the morning of the 6th, to petition the city government authorities, requesting assistance. Secretary Guo of the city government and Yu Mingde, staff member of the Second Section, received them. Representative Chen Guoliang and others then detailed the significance of their petition, pointing out the various inappropriate measures of Zhu Liancheng and others. As a result, Mr. Yu indicated that the city government had received a communication from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and had ordered the Public Utilities Bureau to fully investigate and report on all matters handled by the Bureau, and then legally negotiate with the British Works Department, with the intention of recovering Chinese rights.

External Instructions

The rickshaw pullers' union received instructions from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday. The original text is copied below: Instructions from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs No. 3114. Original petitioner: Shanghai Rickshaw Pullers' Union. Presentation of a case requesting the Shanghai Municipal Council to hand over the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society to the labor and management of the rickshaw pullers themselves for self-management. The presentation and attachments have been reviewed. A communication has been sent to the Shanghai Municipal Government requesting investigation and verification. You are hereby notified. Attached for safekeeping. April 2nd, 24th year of the Republic of China. Minister Wang.

Rickshaw Puller Suicide

According to news from the union, Liu Dianyuan, a native of Funing, aged 43, earned a living pulling a rickshaw for the Miliji Car Company at No. 88 Dakang Lane in the French Concession. Recently, because rickshaw pullers must register to pull a rickshaw, he went to the rickshaw registration office of the Municipal Council twice to register, but failed to be admitted. The rickshaw puller was disappointed at not being able to register, and unable to pull a rickshaw. The livelihood of his family of five was cut off, causing him indescribable worry. Suddenly, yesterday, he hanged himself in the middle of the night. He has no clothing or coffin. The situation is tragic. His wife, Liu Hu, sought help from the rickshaw pullers' union yesterday afternoon. Chen Guoliang, the general representative of the rickshaw pullers, took the responsibility to find ways to assist in the funeral arrangements.

Planning and Laying Main Drainage Ditches in the Southern and Western Districts of Shanghai 150

In addition to the main drainage ditches that have been built successively along Lujia Hong Road and Pu Zhao Road in the southern and western districts of Shanghai, the roads east of Rihui Port have traditionally relied on open ditches for drainage. Every summer and autumn, stagnant water accumulates in low-lying areas, making it difficult to drain, which directly affects the public health of citizens and indirectly harms the road surface. In view of this, the Municipal Works Bureau presented a proposal to the Municipal Government, which was approved to lay main drainage ditches in Xietu Road (from Manufacturing Bureau Road to Xiaomu Bridge Road), Manufacturing Bureau Road (from Xiqiao Road to Longhua Road), Dapu Road (from Xietu Road to Xie Xu Road), and Jumen Road (from Xie Xu Road to Xietu Road). The work has now begun. After the work is completed, not only can the appearance of the city be expected to be tidy, but also the residents along the road, who have suffered from the lack of a total drainage system in the past, can apply to the Engineering Management Office of the Bureau on Zhonghua Road, pay the fees according to the regulations, and connect to the ditch, which will greatly benefit public health.

The Second Hibiscus Competition Postponed to Winter; Notice from the Municipal Zoo to Bird Owners 151

The Municipal Zoo of this city, in order to stimulate the public's interest in raising birds during this beautiful spring season, has prepared to hold the Second Hibiscus Competition. The competition rules and participation methods were drafted and submitted to the Municipal Education Bureau for approval, and the competition was scheduled to be held on the 14th of this month. Now, many island owners have written to say that the hibiscus is currently in the process of incubating eggs and raising chicks, requesting postponement. After discussion at the park's administrative meeting, it was approved to postpone the event to winter. Yesterday, a notice was sent to all participants, stating: "We hereby inform you that the Second Hibiscus Competition, originally scheduled for April 14th, has been postponed to winter this year due to the majority of bird owners stating that their hibiscus are currently incubating eggs and raising chicks, and requesting postponement. This has been reported to the Municipal Education Bureau for record. We hereby inform you, and hope you will take note."

A Young Child Goes Missing; Kidnappers Interrogated and Sentence Scheduled 153

At noon on the 17th of last month, Xiao Di, the three-year-old son of Zhou Yu, a woman from Jiangbei living in a bungalow on Haizhou Road, was playing near the doorway when he suddenly went missing. Ms. Zhou reported this to the Yangshupu police station, which dispatched detectives to search for him, but without success. Subsequently, detectives Sun Afu and Li Zhenyuan successively apprehended the perpetrators, Meng Ersheng, Jin Shouming, his wife Xia, and Wang Bao (alias Lao Wu) from Anhui, and other persons involved. They were taken to the police station and sent to the First Special District Court for investigation. The other day, Judge Jiang Shuzi visited the Third Criminal Court to conduct a preliminary hearing. Mr. Li Zhishan, a lawyer from the Municipal Council, stated that in the course of the investigation, it was found that the defendant Meng Ersheng was near the victim's home when he saw Xiao Di playing with his older sister. He then devised a plan to send his older sister away to buy cigarettes. He then lured Xiao Di to Jin and his wife's house for temporary custody. Later, through a middleman, he sold Xiao Di to a Li family on Lloyd Road, agreeing on a price of 30 yuan, which was split and spent. However, the location of the Li family's residence could not be verified. The child has not been heard from to this day. He requested strict punishment. When questioned, the defendants shirked responsibility and gave evasive answers. Judge Jiang ruled that they should be returned to custody separately and that the sentence would be scheduled.

Shanghai is able to have its prosperity today, and the hard work of my fellow-villagers from Guangdong should not be forgotten. However, in the past, there was a lack of contact, and people acted on their own, with each dividing its own territory and not communicating with each other, forming a heap of loose sand, which was a major obstacle to the development of our careers. But the past is gone, and the future can be pursued. Shanghai is the center of economics and commerce for the whole country, so everything that happens in Shanghai affects the whole country. Therefore, the fellow-villagers in Shanghai must have a great spirit for the responsibilities they bear. Benefiting others is benefiting ourselves, and loving our country begins with loving our hometown. As the saying goes, "It is difficult to clap with one hand, but easy to lift with many hands." I firmly believe that the future of the association, the happiness of our fellow-villagers, and the revival of the country all depend on our efforts today. I hope that my fellow-villagers will unite as one, and then the future of society, the country, and the nation will be greatly benefited."

Since the preparations began, Mayor Wu and local people from Guangdong have generously agreed to serve as general captain and general staff, so that this membership expansion campaign has been prepared in a short period of time, and we are very pleased to be able to hold the grand opening ceremony today. All that is taught, learned, and done is based on this principle, and then China's rural areas will have hope. A Chauffeur Makes a Scene at the Grand Stage; Many People Injured in a Brutal Fight 159

On the third day of the previous session, at the Shanghai Grand Stage at the intersection of Laobsheng Road and Jiaozhou Road in western Shanghai, a Yancheng native named Cheng Yunqing, who worked as a chauffeur, entered the venue after buying a ticket and went up to the stage to watch the performance. After being driven down by the staff of the venue, Cheng harbored resentment and left. Yesterday, being Sunday, at about 3:30 p.m., when the theater was selling well, Cheng, in order to retaliate, brought Ji Xiaqing and about 20 soldiers of the security team with him, and they rushed into the venue. The staff of the venue asked them to buy tickets. Unexpectedly, after a disagreement, Cheng gave a shout and a full-scale fight began. Iron rods, wooden sticks, benches, and chairs were all used. For a time, the audience fled in droves, and order was greatly disrupted. Fortunately, Inspector Gu of the Laobsheng Road Police Station led the police to the scene and ordered them to stop. However, there were already six injured people lying on the ground. Sun Lihe, the theater's waiter, was severely injured all over his body and was bleeding from his mouth. He was in a dying state. Li Xueyu, Shao Zhishan, and Sheng Guangju, who were also waiters, were all injured in the head, hands, and feet. Du Tingshan, Wang Xianghui, and Hu Fusheng, three members of the security team, were also injured. An ambulance was called and they were all sent to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. The leaders, Cheng and Ji, as well as Song Xibiao, the representative of the theater, were taken back to the Caojiadu Branch for questioning and investigation. It is said that Sun Lihe's injuries are very serious and he may die.

City Sounds 165

Life Bookstore's Special Arrangement for Free Bank Drafts: The Life Bookstore, in view of the difficulties and expenses faced by out-of-town readers in purchasing books and newspapers, has specially concentrated its efforts on handling purchases and subscriptions for all kinds of books and magazines nationwide. It was the earliest to start, and its reputation is most outstanding. Now, to further reduce the burden on readers and strive for convenience and efficiency, it has successively arranged with ten major banks with the widest branch networks nationwide, including "China," "Jiaotong," "Shanghai," "New Mei," "Zhejiang Industrial," "Dalu," "Overseas Chinese," "Juxingcheng," and "Fudian New," to provide free drafts for book purchases, providing meticulous convenience to readers. Moreover, in terms of book prices, except for special-priced pre-orders and other books, all others are offered at a 10% discount from the original publisher's retail price. During this "Reading Movement," the bookstore will also handle the half-price discounted books sold by various bookstores with the same preferential treatment as the original publishers, without adding any handling fees. This saves the time and expense of writing letters and remitting money, effectively making it no different from buying directly from the retail outlets of various original publishers in Shanghai. The bookstore has always strived to bridge cultural gaps, disregarding huge sacrifices, and is set to be a model in the book industry.

Expansion of the Buddhist Bookstore's Retail Department: The Buddhist Bookstore on Jiaozhou Road in this city has seen rapid business growth in recent years. The original retail space is no longer sufficient, so a new retail department has been specially opened at 154 Yuyuan Road (behind Jing'an Temple), in a two-story, double-unit Western-style building. The renovation is now complete, and the official opening ceremony is scheduled for April 8th of the national calendar (i.e., tomorrow). From the 7th to the 9th, a special exhibition hall will be set up to display various Buddhist scriptures, solemn Dharma implements, calligraphy and paintings by famous figures, as well as a model of the Nine Flowers Mountain Netherworld Bell, which was initiated by the Chinese Buddhist Association. All are welcome to visit, and refreshments and scriptures will be provided.

New Invention: Clear Juice Filter: Yang Yefu, founder of the Sanxing Industrial Cooperative in Jishanfang, Yuelaishou, outside the Dadongmen of the South City in this city, has invented a clear juice filter. Since its sale nationwide, it has long been praised by national pharmacies and patients, hence its widespread fame. However, Mr. Yang Yefu, dissatisfied with the slow production of manual manufacturing, which cannot meet the needs of national pharmacies, has devoted several years of effort to careful research and invented an automatic electric manufacturing method. The style is novel, and the output is ten times faster than manual, to meet the needs of national pharmacies across the country.

Baoda Teashop's Exquisite Confectionery: The Baoda Huzhou Teashop, located on Nanshi Station Road, near the Difangting Tram Station, is established by a Huzhou merchant named Zhu. It employs renowned teashop technicians who specialize in making various candies and Huzhou-style pastries, each with a unique flavor. Items such as snowflake dumplings, Huzhou date kernels, and candy crisps are particularly delicious. The prices are very affordable, so buyers praise them unanimously.

Yinxing Dashu Brand Pickles Sold in Shanghai: The various pickles produced by Pingwang Dashun Pickles Factory under the Yinxing Dashu brand, such as radish, soy-sauce pickled melon, assorted vegetables, and chili sauce, have been sold for many years and have earned a solid reputation. To provide convenience for people in Shanghai, the Baoda Huzhou Teashop on Nanshi Station Road in Shanghai has been specially entrusted to be the Shanghai resident manager, offering both retail and wholesale services at very reasonable prices.

Lao Jingfu Silk and Satin Shop to Hold Auction Starting Today: The Lao Jingfu Silk and Satin Shop on Xiaodongmenwai Street in the French Concession, due to the impending expiration of its lease, will hold an auction of all its hundreds of thousands of inventory items, regardless of cost. Silks and satins and embroideries will be sold at discounts ranging from 10% to 60%. All items have been carefully selected, with a myriad of designs. It is expected that the area on Dongmen Road will be bustling with traffic, and customers will be endless.

Free Talk

Feeling After Seeking a Monument 170

— Zang Kejia

There's a peculiar phenomenon in this place: the hustle and bustle is in the west, while the city walls surround a desolate silence. A few scattered households support themselves on this vast land, like sparse morning stars adorning the blue sky. The ground is littered with broken tiles and shattered bricks, remnants of former halls and chambers. Atop the ground lie earthen mounds, crowding together the masters of those chambers. Such a gloomy ancient city seems only fit for listening to the chirping of ghosts on overcast, rainy days.

"When the long-haired rebels captured the city, no one was left alive, with at least ten thousand men, women, and children dying!"

There are no fewer than fifty mass graves inside and outside the city. If each mound contains two thousand dead, then the so-called "ten thousand" wouldn't be an exaggeration. The largest ones are outside the north gate, with two or three long mounds lined up on each side. Men are on the left, women on the right, as if even in death, the sexes must be kept separate. It seems that there is no impediment to the dead, so they can still look at each other as neighbors. In front of each mound stands a stone tablet, explaining how these dead were tricked by the cunning long-haired rebels, who used a feint to draw them from the surrounding villages into the city and capture them all in one fell swoop. But the brilliance of the inscription lies not in its description of the facts, but in its expressions of opinion. It praises the men for upholding the righteous spirit of heaven and earth, able to risk their lives in danger and die without surrendering; and the women, seeing that the rebels had broken into the city and the situation was dire, for their unwavering determination, preferring death to dishonor, hanging themselves, swallowing gold, jumping into wells, or falling from the city walls, with their deaths being tragic and their chastity worthy of emulation—these sentences should be highlighted. This article was written after the event. The author must have been a renowned scholar, seizing on such a good topic and naturally wanting to showcase his talent under bright windows, clean tables, and the leisurely daylight. As for whether these unfortunate dead, in the face of imminent disaster, with no time to spare for the terror of death and the struggle for life, truly held onto loyalty and chastity in their hearts, it seems quite questionable. When it comes to suicide, it can only be explained as an attempt to avoid the pain of seeking death.

There are plenty of cover-ups in the world, but exposing them seems to spoil the fun. The inscription was not written for the dead, but for the living to see. The phrase "chastity worthy of emulation" makes it clear that the living are being told to learn from the dead. If all the men in the world become loyal and righteous, and all the women can steadfastly maintain their chastity, then the world can naturally enjoy lasting peace and stability, and the emperor will have an empire that lasts for generations. Understanding this, one can naturally understand the reason why "imperial order" monuments are found all over the world.

Recollections of Impressions of Japan 171

— Guang Huai

It was in the spring of 1930 when a group of us young people were preparing to depart from Shanghai. Everyone was happy—especially myself, being poor and absolutely without the means to study abroad.

Those who travel by ship for the first time always feel a bit uneasy. Fortunately, we were traveling first class, not third class, and there is a clear difference between the two. When the ship arrived in Nagasaki, many Japanese plainclothes detectives rushed into our cabins, looking around as if tigers were searching for people to eat. Luckily, they didn't swallow me whole. This was my first impression of Japan. Later, when my classmates and I were returning home and passing through the Philippines, we were refused permission to land by customs inspectors, and this first impression resurfaced in my mind. After landing, friends took us sightseeing, and unintentionally, a friend pointed out the former Chinese concession, which greatly surprised me. This surprise was unavoidable for someone like me who was still overly enthusiastic and had not yet been cured by correct thinking. However, it later transformed into a driving force that propelled me to explore more deeply. Our tour of Nagasaki was superficial, as we had to catch the train to Tokyo in order to board our original ship to America on time in Yokohama.

My observations in Tokyo and Yokohama were indeed crucial for my intellectual transformation. What we saw in Tokyo (and of course, there were things we didn't see) was indeed beautiful and clean. The streets of Yokohama were also built according to the latest designs. Our guide told us that Yokohama had been reduced to ashes during the previous great earthquake, but in less than five years, the new Yokohama was even more magnificent than the old one. The trains from Tokyo to Yokohama ran extremely punctually, and people boarded without pushing and shoving.

After boarding the original ship from Yokohama, the seas were calm, just like what Su Dongpo described in his "Ode to the Red Cliff": "Drifting on a reed boat, across the vast expanse." With nothing to do on the ship, I began to digest the materials I had observed in Japan. I thought Japan was indeed more advanced than us, with its beautiful Tokyo and Yokohama. But where did this progress come from? During the Sui Dynasty, they sent many people to China to learn applied technologies, such as textiles. During the Tang Dynasty, entire groups of students came to the Chinese capital to study the classics. Even today, the attire of their people still bears the remnants of the Tang Dynasty. Let's not even mention those ancient events. Before the Meiji Restoration, the status of Chinese studies was far above that of Western studies, and China's national power was also greater than Japan's at that time. Why, then, in less than a century, did the historical trajectory completely reverse? I had to find a satisfactory answer to this question, or I wouldn't be at peace.

Naturally, one adopts the method they are most familiar with to solve problems. At that time, I was an idealist and had read a book about Japan written by an idealist who was also an expert on Japan. I thought that all of Japan's modern progress was due to what was called the Yamato national character. But aren't the Japanese all short and nimble, mostly with a bit of the samurai spirit, and willing to take risks? However, such an answer was too simplistic for me. I thought again: agility, willingness to take risks, and the samurai spirit are not necessarily unique to the Japanese. It is true that the Ming Dynasty pirates colluded with Japanese pirates and constantly harassed the coastal provinces of China, but in the early Ming Dynasty, Chinese pirates also adventured southward to harass Southeast Asia, ruling over some of its tribes and establishing commercial relations between China and Southeast Asia. It is true that Japan has Bushido, but hasn't China had chivalrous heroes throughout its history? Moreover, we have many facts that can show that Japanese samurai in many ways directly imitated Chinese knights. It is true that Japan has the commendable military achievements of Toyotomi Hideyoshi, but compared with the military achievements of China's prosperous dynasties, it is only insignificant.

If we say that the advantages of the so-called Yamato national character are biological advantages, if we say that the Yamato people have physiological structures that are better than ours, then we would ask: why did they still have to come to China to learn the most basic life skills during the Sui and Tang dynasties? Why, just over a hundred years ago, did they still worship China and view China as superior to itself?

As far as the knowledge revealed to us by biology is concerned, changes in biological structures are gradual and require a long period of time. Human beings who have not yet broken away from the animal state did not know how much time it took to abandon their quadrupedal behavior. The two front feet became two hands that were freed from walking. The increase in brain weight is also the result of long-term engagement in mental labor. Although we can sometimes find mutation phenomena in the biological world, it is a qualitative change formed by the accumulation of many quantitative changes and is also limited by time. The Japanese of today are certainly not more biologically superior to their ancestors in the Sui and Tang dynasties, or their close ancestors a hundred years ago, because no magic can transform the physiological structure of the Yamato people in such a short period. It can be seen that it is utterly untenable for idealists to explain Japan's progress based on the so-called advantages of the national character.

The more I reasoned, the more I ran into a dead end. Finally, I abandoned the idealist standpoint and adopted a materialist standpoint to think. But the materialism I knew at that time was limited to the geographical determinism proposed by Liang Shuming in his "Eastern and Western Cultures and Their Philosophies," which is a branch of mechanical materialism. Following Brooke's suggestion, I thought that Japan's progress came from its superior geographical situation—from its good harbors, from the barren geology that forced the people to work hard. But this explanation still left a big loophole. The changes in terrain and geology are also gradual over a long period of time. If the geology and terrain of Japan in the Sui and Tang dynasties could differ from the present so much as to produce different cultures and civilizations, we cannot say that the geographical conditions in the less than a century from the Meiji Restoration to the present could have changed to the point where the Japan before and after are like two different countries. A major earthquake can cause several islands to completely sink and several islands to float from the mountains and seas, or a sudden climate change can give birth to or destroy some of the animals and plants on which humans depend for survival, thereby changing the entire lifestyle of the residents, but Japan has not experienced such shocks and historical changes in the past hundred years. If geographical changes can explain Japan's progress, then why has China been struggling in the transition between the old and the new during the same period, even though China's geographical environment has not been without changes? If we say that Japan's geographical changes are towards the superior side, then since they are both geographical changes, why does China's trend towards the inferior side?

The materialism I understood at the time was just a very vague environmental determinism. I used it to explain Japan's progress, but this explanation could not satisfy me because it left several questions that could not be answered in this way. When I studied further, I realized how to fill the loopholes in my previous thinking. It turns out that humans who have not broken away from the animal state are, like animals, subject to the environment. They can only adapt to the external nature, and their lives are completely determined by the external natural environment. But when human history began, that is, when humans could manufacture and use labor tools, they broke away from the animal state. They were still affected by the external natural environment, but they could use their own invented, manufactured, and used labor tools to control the external nature. They can ask the external nature to adapt to themselves to varying degrees, and this degree depends on the level of social labor technology—that is, the level of labor tool system. The reason why Japan a hundred years ago was so different from Japan today is none other than the role of machinery and science there.

Speaking of this, we cannot help but sweat for the present China, which is blinded by anti-science and machine awareness!

新加拉惹輪中 172

— 斐兒

We paused for one night at the customhouse of the Lu River. The next day, a K.P.M. company steamer was fully loaded with cargo, and in the evening, it set sail on a ship called "Singaradja."

A steamer traveling twelve miles per hour felt very slow to the passengers. Moreover, the Lu River kept making turns, constantly curbing the desire to see the sea again. Having been confined to the lonely K. area for three years, shaking hands with a giant of modern civilization—a ship—brought unspeakable joy. Furthermore, a pair of eyes that were once sharp, dulled by the dim kerosene lamps inside the low huts, were suddenly exposed to the bright electric lights of the ship, feeling as if one had leaped from the eighteenth or nineteenth century to the twentieth century, experiencing novelty and delight.

But as soon as the ship reached the Lerong fishing area, the Lu River was swallowed by the sea, and darkness shrouded the earth. The "sea love" that was felt from the coast of Singapore and the coast of Tanjung Bungah (Penang) could no longer be savored, truly a "lasting disappointment!"

Beyond the small circle of electric light, the sea was all darkness. The stars twinkled in the high sky, offering no power to the light. Few passengers were on board, and even fewer were awake, so the loneliness deepened. Only the roar of the machinery pierced the eardrums, a force of relentless propulsion that commanded admiration!

Suddenly, a Dutch teenager on deck began to sing loudly and play an instrument. Just as I wanted to receive beautiful melodies from the vast sea, the singing and music stopped, followed by dancing. A Dutch young woman, like a newlywed on her honeymoon, whispered in the Dutch teenager's ear, and the lonely dance stopped abruptly.

The power of the environment brought complete silence to the ship.

While Mr. Lin and I were preparing our bedding, a middle-aged man with a dark brown face suddenly emerged. He used a friendly and approachable attitude, constantly chatting with us in a low voice. Mr. Lin used a sophisticated tone to deal with him. Eventually, I realized that this gentlemanly and "boss"-like middle-aged man was actually trying to proselytize. Mr. Lin continued to placate him, but I tilted my ear to listen to the majestic roar of the sea.

The preacher walked away seemingly empty-handed, and an unbridled wild horse began to gallop in my heart: young people who had lost their lives and happiness from fervent beliefs over the years flashed through my mind one by one. A wave of manic feeling passed through my nerves, and I thought "God" should just be kicked into the sea.

Mr. Lin, covered in a red blanket, was planning his affairs, but I was thinking of "Bomb" (a friend) lying dying in the Asahan hospital. The sea beat against the iron plates of the ship's hull, and my heart was gnawed by the world's faiths.

The bow of the ship was illuminated by a dim light, and I thought faith should only listen to the light indicated by the ship's bow. At sea, life is exceptionally obscure; even breathing can be swallowed by deathly silence. Let the ship's rudder guide me to my destination!

The preacher's face and his mellifluous words completely slipped out of my comforted mind, and the night ship surged forward in the dark sea, surging forward.

峇魯村的早晨 173

— 雷鐵鳴

Baru Village was quiet, hidden in the gray fog…

The horizon was already shimmering with the color of dawn, with clusters of pale white clouds moving across the hazy sky. In the lonely and vast mountains and fields, a slight morning breeze blew gently, bringing a hint of tropical coolness.

In the coconut groves and banyan trees, birds began to chirp and sing happily, hopping about. Wild insects in the grass also hissed and buzzed softly, wriggling.

"Cock-a-doodle-doo…"

The rooster's crow, like a joyful cry, sharply pierced the silence of the morning. Gradually, Baru Village heard the sounds of children crying, women talking, old people coughing, and faint footsteps…

On the mist-shrouded riverbank, the sparse shadows of fishermen moved about. Before the sun rose, they had to rush to the mouth of the sea. One by one, the fishing boats rowed toward the winding river surface, carrying the sound of *squish squish* of the oars.

"Woo!——"

The factory siren on the Mount of Petroleum howled, and its terrifying echo, like a lion's roar, awakened the entire sleeping Baru Village.

"Ding-dong! Ding-dong!…" Then, the large bronze bell in the bell tower on the high slope of Baru Village also rang.

"Sima, get up! The siren has already sounded!"

"Aaron! Do you hear the bell ringing?"

The women were nudging their husbands, calling out urgently. The men, having just recovered from their fatigue, opened their bloodshot, sleepy eyes and hurriedly climbed out of bed.

At this time, all the men, women, children, and old people in the village got up; they mechanically went through the motions, some brewing coffee and tea for their husbands, some busy tidying up fruit stalls, some grinding axes with a rustling sound, and some scolding their children, while others went naked to the well to take a cold shower.

In this Baru Village, filled with noise and vitality, the people heard the long wail of the mountain siren for the second time.

The sky was filled with cotton-like white clouds, and a faint red shadow of the sun was already glimmering in the eastern corner. The hazy mist had completely dissipated, and the surroundings were filled with clear, warm air!

On the flat stone bridge and the rugged pebble road, the number of pedestrians gradually increased, one, two, three; in this crowd there were strong workers, agile women, lively children, sturdy old men, peddlers carrying baskets, woodcutters carrying ropes and axes, road workers carrying shovels…

"Garsin, good morning!"

"Oh, it's you! Alie Napea."

"Liya, has Garzang's illness gotten better yet? Too many chilies!"

Whether men, women, old or young, they greeted each other, their faces showing warm and sincere smiles, as if they had forgotten their fatigue and toil. Walking, they left Baru Village behind, each heading toward their own factories, deep mountains, forests, markets, vegetable patches…

The sun, like a piece of burning charcoal, rose and kissed the floating red clouds passionately, and the beautiful golden light shone all over the distant and nearby coconut groves, rooftops, fields, streams, and the entire Baru Village.

"Woo woo——"

Thick black smoke was already billowing from the oil derricks on the Mount of Petroleum; and the crowd trudging forward on the pebble road also gradually disappeared in the blood-red sunlight.

The morning sun peeked out from the treetops, and the warm light slowly became scorching. From the rooftops of the "attap houses" in Baru Village, sparse wisps of smoke floated lightly; the women were busy cooking, washing clothes, and gathering firewood; a frail old man sat under the bamboo fence feeding chickens, and several unweaned children were singing mountain songs; there were a few dogs wandering around in the coconut grove; and a flock of ducks floated on the stream…

The Malay village of Baru, at this moment, returned to the same silence as in the middle of the night.

巨卿先生（九） 174

— 柯靈

"In these times, it's really impossible for us small businesses to say anything. They, the big shots, love to quarrel, and the unlucky ones are the bystanders. I'm like a mute eating bitter herbs, who am I going to appeal to, to that great and impartial sky? Luckily, there are many empty houses on the street now. The classrooms in the school, no matter how precious they are, I won't rent them anymore. It's hard to do business these days. If it weren't for my big and small children needing to eat, I really wouldn't open this kind of lousy store."

He paused for a moment.

"Because of this matter, the school still hasn't started classes. The students are all wandering around like wild ghosts all day long. I really don't know when it will end. We, the little ones, have decided not to let him go back to school anymore. That's why I came to discuss it with you, sir, and ask you to take him in."

Mr. Juqing's heart began to pound rapidly, but he tried hard to maintain his composure. He agreed to Mr. Fu Dianwang's request, wrinkling his brow and saying:

"Running a school in the first place is just a joke. The children don't study all day long, they just focus on doing gymnastics and singing folk songs. What kind of behavior is that! Now it's even more of a mess."

That night, when Mr. Juqing returned home, he was so happy that a long-unseen smile spread across his face.

Taking advantage of this opportunity, Mr. Juqing also approached several other places. And he ran out every day to inquire whether the storm at the district-run elementary school had spread further.

When people in power fight, there is usually a third party in power who comes out to "mediate." This storm lasted for seven or eight days, and finally subsided. When Principal Zhang Shaoxiong announced to the students that classes would resume immediately, the number of students listening had decreased by almost half. At the same time, the several private schools in the town all seemed like dying lamps that had been refueled, showing a little bit of life.

The most successful one was Mr. Juqing. The result of this storm was that he gained six or seven more students. Everyone read aloud with drawn-out voices, and the sound of reading was actually a bit noisy.

In early February, the eaves and corners of the houses were filled with dreamlike east winds.

Following the warming weather, Mr. Juqing's heart seemed to have a bit of a "spring revival" too. Compared to before, although the current situation still had many shortcomings, he already felt content.

Special Issue of the Reading Movement Conference Sponsored by the Chinese Cultural Construction Association
