Manifesto of the Reading Movement Conference 176

Any nation that can soar in the world has two wings: one is superior spiritual power, and the other is superior material power. The so-called spiritual power is intelligence, while material power includes physical strength, wealth, and material resources as major elements. Current collectivists tend to emphasize material power while neglecting spiritual power, which is a big mistake. Because if there is no spiritual power to dominate, then even if there is strong physical strength, abundant wealth, and numerous material resources, they will fall into a state of no control, no organization, and no management. Once you want to use them on a large-scale nation, you will find that this material power is just a pile of loose sand, not a united and solidified cement, and you can only let others defeat them one by one.

The only way to increase spiritual power is to seek knowledge, and to seek knowledge, you must read. Books are the sum of inherent culture. We can achieve the effect of reviewing the old and knowing the new by reading books. Books are the crystallization of Western culture. We can get a ladder to catch up by reading books. The reason why our nation cannot soar in the world, and even its survival is greatly threatened, is largely due to not reading books and not seeking knowledge. Not reading books and not seeking knowledge means that the light of wisdom cannot illuminate the dangers around us, and the power of the spirit cannot control our own material resources, so it is no wonder that China will become a neo-colony of foreign countries. Now we invite everyone to participate in the reading movement. Its greatest purpose is to hope that everyone can prepare more useful knowledge to control, organize, and manage their own material power, and to fight for the survival of our nation.

Some people think that what the country and the nation need now are airplanes, battleships, cannons, and bombs, not books that are not worth a penny. In fact, airplanes, battleships, cannons, and bombs are certainly useful, but the knowledge of manufacturing and using these airplanes, battleships, cannons, and bombs is even more useful. If there is no knowledge to manufacture airplanes, battleships, cannons, and bombs, how can airplanes, battleships, cannons, and bombs be produced? If there is no knowledge to use airplanes, battleships, cannons, and bombs, then even if there are airplanes, battleships, cannons, and bombs, what is the use? From this, can we not see that intellectual power, which belongs to the spirit, is more important than physical strength, wealth, and material resources, which belong to matter?

Didn't the French say that their recovery of Alsace-Lorraine was the power of elementary school teachers? The textbooks in the hands of elementary school teachers can be used as magic weapons to recover lost territories, so wouldn't books other than elementary school textbooks have even greater effects? Then why don't we also hurry up and read books to seek knowledge?

Dear compatriots, please move the time spent on nothing to reading books, and move the money spent on useless things to buying books. We must know that organizing a country with a majority of uneducated people is more dangerous than using rotten ropes to drive six horses. Now uneducated people are all over the country, what do we rely on to fight for the survival of the nation?

We dare to assert that whether it is to enrich the lives of the people, to develop the national economy independently, or to fight for the survival of the nation, it is closely related to the rise and fall of learning, and the rise and fall of learning is linked to whether people are willing to read books and seek knowledge, so reading is what China needs at this time and in this place.

怎樣讀書 177

— 樊仲雲

"How to Read" is the most common topic, just like "How to Eat." Everyone who reads probably knows it. For example, eye-to-eye, mouth-to-mouth, heart-to-heart, and hand-to-hand are all old sayings that don't need to be repeated. Even how to write notes, how to add lines and marks, etc., are all well-known. Therefore, I will just write about my personal reading experience here.

I am ashamed to say that I have never systematically read any books. Half of the reason is that I had to work for a living when I was still studying, and I didn't have a whole period of time; half of the reason is that I didn't have the spirit of hard research like the ancients. My reading is mostly based on my own temporary interest, or initiated by the introduction of friends. Therefore, I usually just browse ordinary books and leave it at that. Only if I find that a book is worth rereading after browsing it, I will not only select the main points of each paragraph and add money, circles, or dots, but also take notes of the main points of each paragraph on the book. Because taking the main points of each paragraph forces me to have careful thoughts about the books I read. Through such repeated thinking, after reading the whole book, I have a considerable concept of the general content. When I write an article and need to refer to it, I open the book I have read, and by looking at the main points I have taken on the eyebrows, I can easily find the material I need. I think this method seems better than writing notes, because it saves time. Of course, this is just my personal opinion. If there is more time, then putting in more effort is always more beneficial than being lazy.

My reading method is to make circles and marks on the book, and then add marginal notes and extract the main points. Therefore, when I encounter books borrowed from others or from the library, I feel that it is impossible to do so. So, even though I have read the book, I often have to buy a copy myself in order to extract the main points. However, because I have already read it, the work of marking it is often put aside. Because I have not read this book carefully, and after a while, when I reread it, I often find it very unfamiliar, as if I have never read it before. This makes me feel that it is not enough to just read a book. After reading it, there must be thinking and note-taking, so that the content of the book can be used by me. In other words, this is still the old method of eye-to-eye, heart-to-heart, and hand-to-hand, but I have come to know this old method through my own experience.

Another experience is that I think that when reading history and geography, and even when reading newspapers and magazines, it is best to have a map at the same time. Often, with the help of maps, I can understand and remember facts more easily. Especially when reading history, it takes a lot of effort to remember ancient place names. If you can compare the present with the past with a map, it is very easy to remember.

Also, because I work in a bookstore, I can often go to the library to browse the books I want to read. Naturally, I have read a lot, but it has made me realize the vastness of the sea of learning. There are many books that I have only browsed through the table of contents and the preface, but I have still gotten a general idea of them. Therefore, I feel that the opportunity to read is also very important for young people. Now, libraries no longer have the freedom of entry and exit as they used to, but in order to expand my understanding of pictures, I have to go to Chinese and foreign bookstores to browse books, which has become a kind of pastime like watching movies. Sometimes, when I encounter a good book, I will buy it back, considering my finances. However, when my pockets are empty, even if there is a book, I have to leave reluctantly, and it is really uncomfortable at that time.

As for reading foreign languages, my experience is probably like this: because I learned English and Japanese on my own, and my purpose at the time was to read books, I didn't care much about the pronunciation, and I didn't even care about writing. My intention was only to understand the true meaning of the sentences. But to understand the true meaning, it is not enough to just know the new words and explain the sentences. So, I used this to practice my translation, which allowed me to think and savor each word and sentence carefully. What I read was mostly literary works in English with Japanese translations and notes. Therefore, I had to explain English with Japanese, and understand Japanese with English, and compare and contrast them from both sides to recognize their meaning. I would like to use this method to learn German on my own, but after the age of thirty, although I can find time, the spirit of reading that I had when I was young has greatly diminished. As a result, I still cannot get into the door of German. From this, we can know that in addition to "how to read", you also need to have the spirit of reading.

怎樣研究哲學 178

— 葉靑

The special issue of the Reading Movement asks me to write a short article on the study of philosophy. I have always advocated research, especially the study of philosophy. But I have never written about this topic before. So, I might as well take this opportunity to provide some methodological advice to those who study philosophy.

I think the phrase "studying philosophy" contains two meanings. One is to understand existing philosophy, and the other is to establish a new philosophy. The former is preparatory work, and the latter is pioneering work. Strictly speaking, only the latter is worthy of being called "studying philosophy", while the former is just learning philosophy or acquiring philosophical knowledge.

Therefore, in the study of philosophy, I will also divide it into two to discuss, starting with the first one.

(1) Read an introduction to philosophy. This is necessary. Otherwise, you won't even know what philosophy is. An introduction to philosophy tells you general philosophical knowledge. So, you should understand this first.

(2) Read the history of philosophy. Philosophy is divided into schools, and it is also divided into families. Those who study philosophy cannot be ignorant of the doctrines of the various schools and families in the past. How can it be said that the essence of philosophy is the theory of this school and that school, this family and that family, and there is no common and definite content at all?

(3) Philosophy. Choose a school or family of philosophy that you think is correct from the history of philosophy to discuss. Collect as many philosophical books of that school or family as possible. You must understand its origin, development, and demise, so that you can master the words of one family.

(4) What is correct philosophy? I think it is the philosophy that is consistent with science. What is the philosophy that is consistent with science? In the first part II of my book "Critique of Zhang Rongsun's Philosophy" (published by Xin Ken Bookstore), there is a clear and detailed explanation, which I don't have the space to mention here.

Now let's talk about the second method of research.

(1) To create a philosophy, you must first pay attention to the historical development of philosophy. A family of philosophy is a set of logic, a school of philosophy is a set of logic, and a history of philosophy is also a set of logic. And creating a philosophy is the unfolding of the logic of the history of philosophy. Then, how can you unfold its logic if you don't understand the development of philosophy?

(2) In fact, this is just telling us where to put our efforts. How to unfold logic? I think you can only read the history of philosophy carefully and do deep thinking. So, the method is nothing else, here it is nothing more than these three: first, think; second, think; third, think.

(3) What kind of thinking? I think you need to have a holistic, historical, and logical view of the development of philosophy. In the beginning, you need to start with one era at a time. The method is to grasp the characteristics of each era. And in the meantime, you must always pay attention to the overall thread. You must do this in order to understand what problems need to be solved when this set of logic comes to our modern times.

(4) How to solve it? Appeal to science. Even if you have obtained a solution to the problem from thinking, you must also seek evidence from science. Today, you cannot have philosophical theory without leaving science. The era of purely thinking and establishing a philosophical era from philosophical thinking is over.

(5) What science? In terms of cosmology and cosmology, it is natural science; in terms of life theory, it is social science. And in the former, physics and biology are the most important, and in the latter, economics and sociology are the most important. This naturally does not mean that other subjects do not need attention. Philosophy should use science as the material to build it.

(6) How to study science? Not the research of scientists, that is, technical research, but should take the approach of philosophers. In other words, it is to conduct purely theoretical exploration of science. Therefore, you should pay special attention to scientific discoveries with theoretical significance, such as the atomic theory, electron theory, quantum theory, theory of relativity, theory of evolution, etc.

(7) Moreover, I think that philosophy today is fundamentally unified with science, that is, the form of general theory or conclusion of science from the descriptive stage, the explanatory stage, to the highest theoretical stage. The philosophy of philosophy has disappeared, and there is only the philosophy of science (see my book "Where is Philosophy Going?" also published by Xin Ken Bookstore). Studying philosophy is to recognize it, elucidate it, and develop it.

The above two methods are both special methods, which are the same as studying general knowledge subjects. This is described in detail in my article "How to Study Theory". That article is in the second issue of the second volume of the twentieth century, which is sold by Xin Ken Bookstore, so I won't repeat it here.

Finally, I want to declare that because of the limited space, I cannot say everything, and at the same time there are things that I don't fully mean. I will discuss the method of philosophy in another article later. But it can be asserted that these short words can be used as a reference for people.

My Reading Experience 179

— Cai Yuanpei

I began reading when I was just over ten years old; now, nearly sixty years have passed. Except for major illnesses or other special reasons, there has hardly been a day when I haven't read something. Yet, I have not achieved much, and this is because my reading methods were flawed. I will write down a rough outline of my ineffective methods, which can serve as a warning to others.

My first shortcoming was the inability to focus. When I first started reading, I read mostly old books, primarily those dealing with textual research and literary composition. My preferences in textual research leaned towards exegesis and philosophical principles, while I lacked patience for institutions and nomenclature. In literary composition, I favored prose and was not particularly keen on parallel prose or poetry. However, I was ashamed to be ignorant of anything, so I read everything. I even studied mathematics and medicine books, but I never mastered any of them. I once intended to compile a "Phonetic and Semantic Exegesis of the Shuowen Jiezi," and also a "Grand Interpretation of the Gongyang Commentary on the Spring and Autumn Annals," but neither came to fruition. As for my literary works, not only was there not a single piece of parallel prose or poetry worth preserving, but even my prose was too commonplace. After the age of forty, I began learning German, and later French, but I never diligently memorized vocabulary or practiced grammar. Instead, I just devoured books, so I still cannot write a passable essay or give a short speech. After entering university in Germany and attending lectures, I listened to everything: history of philosophy, history of literature, history of civilization, psychology, aesthetics, history of art, and ethnology. At that time, I also began to read a mishmash of reference books related to these subjects. Later, I勉forced myself to narrow my focus, concentrating mainly on aesthetics and art history, supplemented by ethnology. However, I could never bring myself to give up other types of books entirely. Therefore, I wanted to translate a book on aesthetics and compile a comparative ethnology, but neither came to fruition.

My second shortcoming was the inability to take notes diligently. My reading was driven by a kind of egoism, I didn't bother to seek out the shortcomings in the books I read. I focused on what I found useful or appealing. This in itself wasn't necessarily bad, but my flaw was that, while I paid attention to these points while reading, I often didn't take the time to jot them down or make special notes in the book in the interest of speed reading. If I later wanted to recall something, except for German books with detailed indexes, it was almost impossible to find in the other books. Although there are now people in China who compile "indexes" and specialized dictionaries, which are gradually increasing, making it easier to search, everyone has their own focus, and ordinary indexes cannot be as convenient as one's own notes. I once saw Mr. Hu Shih, during a certain period, often carrying one or two thread-bound books when going out, leafing through them on trains or in other moments of leisure, and marking useful material by folding the corner or making a note in pencil. I imagine that he would then make a copy when he returned home. I remember a notebook saying that Wang Yuyang, when reading, would write down new and brilliant allusions or phrases on paper strips and stick them on the walls of his study, reading them frequently, and then removing them when he was familiar with them, replacing them with new ones. That is why he remembered so much. Although this is a literary trick, why couldn't it be imitated in science? Because I have always been too lazy to write, I have not achieved anything.

I have experienced many inconveniences from my reading shortcomings and have written them down specifically, hoping that readers will learn from my mistakes. First, be able to focus; second, be able to take notes. This will surely bring many benefits.

How to Study Economics 180

— Jiang Bai

1. Why Study Economics?

In the realm of social sciences, the term "economics" occupies an extremely important position. In primitive societies, uncivilized peoples, whether they engage in fishing, hunting, or animal husbandry, all demonstrate a pursuit of material goods to satisfy their material needs. In modern society, where the material lives of individuals and families are consistently improving, the relationship with economics becomes even more intimate. In modern nations, all legislative and administrative actions cannot be separated from an economic backdrop. In recent international affairs, discussions of relationships and cooperation must take economics as a prerequisite. Thus, economics is not only a subject that specialized scholars must study in detail, but also one that the general public should understand in outline to adapt to modern society.

2. Materials for Studying Economics

The materials for studying economics are complex, but if scientific methods are used to synthesize them, they can be categorized into the following. Beginners in economics should classify and categorize them, studying them in sequence, from the simple to the complex, and it will be easy to grasp their essence. Once you have a path for research and a considerable understanding of economic science, you can also find a system within the following categories that suits your interests and conduct further research. This is also acceptable.

(3) Studying from the perspective of economic policy: Economic policy is the expression of economic thinkers and the method of economic scholars' research results, which governments of various countries now adopt as mutual assistance or antagonistic means. Economic policies can be further divided into monetary policy, tariff policy, international trade policy, and so on. However, the main driving forces behind them are no more than the following three: (1) Free trade policy; (2) Protective tariff policy; (3) Neo-mercantilist policy.

(4) Studying from the perspective of economic problems: Economic problems can be international or domestic. When you reach this point in your studies, you will have a considerable understanding of economic principles, economic thought, and economic policy. For example, take the recent silver problem; this problem involves a part of monetary theory in economic principles, and both exchange and distribution must be discussed; it also involves a part of international trade policy, and the economic conditions of various countries must also be understood. To understand the matter thoroughly or to find a result, it is certainly not something that a beginner in economics can accomplish. In addition to this, there are many economic topics, such as tariff issues, the American gold bill issue, the maintenance of the gold standard by European countries such as France, Belgium, and Italy, and the problem of inflation in China. Depending on the scholar's interests, they can all be studied to solve domestic and international economic panic and seek an effective rescue strategy.

4. Methods of Studying Economics:

(1) Studying from the perspective of economic principles: Economic principles focus on explaining or arguing whether principles are appropriate; they include four major parts: production theory, exchange theory, distribution theory, and consumption theory. Any economic phenomenon in modern society is within these four parts; if it does not fall into one, it falls into another. Beginners in economics should first understand these principles; those who study economic theory must pursue these principles.

(2) Studying from the perspective of economic thought: Economic thought is the source of the entire field of economics. Some are fragmented economic views. However, these fragmented ideas are often systematic, organized, and promoted into great economic theories. Some include the entire aspect of economics. Although economic thought is not entirely economic theory, it is the existence of economic thought that leads to the current economic organization. To understand the economic phenomena in Europe since the 16th century, there are two major trends: liberalism and nationalism. The former believes that the economy is driven by individual initiative and that the state should not interfere with its development; therefore, some call it individualism. The latter believes that social wealth should be controlled by state power, and individual freedom of action is reduced to zero, whether in production, exchange, distribution, or consumption. Therefore, some call it interventionism. What is now called socialism is also included. A table is listed below to facilitate browsing and research:

Now that the materials for economics are known to be observed separately, one must also have a method to study them in order to understand them thoroughly and achieve complete results. The methods that the ancients used to study are introduced below.

(1) Analytical method or deductive method: Classical economists used this method to study economics. Some start from psychology and deduce various economic laws from individual desires and needs, forming the psychological school of economists today. Some use mathematical or algebraic methods to deduce, so they are also called the mathematical school of economists.

(2) Method of factual observation: Economists who use this method focus on the evolution of facts and ignore abstract analysis, which is the opposite of classical economists. This can be further divided into three groups:

A. Direct observation method—French Leplay school;

B. Historical research method—German Hiletant Koscher Sctomlier;

C. Economic observation method—Most modern legislators belong to this category.

Since the research methods of the ancients are such, which one should we adopt? The former emphasizes analysis, so it inevitably overlooks the changes in human life and the motivation of human needs for material goods. The latter only pays attention to facts, which may be too biased and lack objectivity. If we want to study, we should choose the strengths of both and use both methods; first observe economic phenomena, then examine historical facts, and then use deductive methods to analyze. In this way, it will not be difficult to solve any economic material.

(5) The objects and hopes of studying economics:

The various economic objects of production, exchange, distribution, and consumption are nothing more than individuals, society, the state, and the international community. After our research, we should at least have some hopes. As for individuals, they should be thrifty in order to increase production with savings obtained from their labor. If everyone does this, the social wealth can also increase. As for society, both labor and capital should help each other so that social productivity will not be reduced due to conflicts, and everyone's material life will gradually improve. As for the country, the government should adopt interventionism and implement controlled economy, so that the country's wealth production and wealth distribution will have an overall plan, so as not to ignore one thing and lose another, causing social disturbances or the aggression of great powers. As for the international community, only by implementing economic cooperation and economic advancement can world struggle be eliminated, and human happiness can be truly improved. Otherwise, if one country is rich and another is poor, or if the material development of the east neighbors and the material deficiencies of the west neighbors, such a畸形abnormal phenomenon is only the misfortune of mankind.

How to Study History 181

— He Bingsong

This topic is very broad and cannot be covered in a few words. Now, I can only offer a few humble opinions on the purpose and attitude of reading history for readers to consider.

History is a record of human past events, similar to our personal memories. Personal experience relies on memory to guide us on our path forward; human past events rely on records to guide our direction. At the same time, reading history not only allows us to understand the different characteristics and trends of Chinese and foreign cultures but also allows us to understand that Chinese and foreign cultures are constantly changing, which is enough to increase our courage to move forward.

Another point is that all modern scholars, whether they are writers or chemists, must have a "historical attitude." The so-called historical attitude is to "thoroughly investigate the origins" of everything. Only when the origins are understood can we see the whole picture of the matter. For example, when治理 governing a river, we must start by surveying the upstream. If we only work on the downstream, we will not get any results. The same is true if we want to understand the content and value of all human affairs in society. Relying solely on the present without tracing the origins will lead to the arbitrary knowledge of two-fifths while ignorant of one-tenth, which is not enough. This attitude is the most important attitude in modern scholarship, and it can only be cultivated by reading history.

Studying history is like studying other sciences. We need to be both broad and deep. Being broad expands our understanding of human past events, and being deep concentrates our attention on a certain era, region, or aspect of history. Breadth leads to greatness, and depth leads to profundity. In general, we should focus on breadth when reading history and strive for depth when we have the capacity. Breadth is the cultivation of common sense, and depth is specialized research. When studying any academic field, it is always advisable to first have a wealth of common sense before becoming a specialized expert.

Studying history also has a secondary benefit: eliminating prejudices. Therefore, modern scientific historians can always strive to eliminate their own prejudices. Because writing history with prejudices easily reverses right and wrong, reversing the order of importance. This loses the calm, impartial attitude of modern scientists. Historical works that first establish a proposition and then gather historical facts to prove that proposition can also be regarded as works that promote personal propositions. We should not have prejudices when writing history ourselves, and we must first see if the author has prejudices when reading other people's works.

We are all Chinese and should know something about Chinese history. We are also modern people and should also read some foreign history. Reading Chinese history allows us to understand the reasons why the oldest and largest civilization in the world has been preserved. Reading foreign history allows us to understand why our own ancient civilization is now being oppressed by foreign countries. At the same time, reading Chinese history can make us understand what our culture is and how to transform it to suit modern needs. Reading foreign history can make us understand what Western culture is and how to introduce it to China and make it Chinese, so that it suits China's needs.

In short, all modern Chinese youth should read some Chinese and foreign history to increase essential common sense, cultivate a "historical attitude," deeply understand the similarities and differences between Chinese and foreign cultures, and the path to the revival of national culture, and be determined to be a healthy member who creates a Chinese-based culture.

Education News

Ministry of Education Revises and Promulgates Two Regulations for Graduation Examinations for Middle School and Normal School Students 182

The Ministry of Education will revise the regulations for graduation examinations for middle school students and normal school students and issue orders to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities. The orders were seen in yesterday's newspaper. The two regulations are recorded below:

(1) Revised Regulations for Graduation Examinations for Middle School Students

Article 1 The educational administrative agencies of each province, city, and district shall, for the graduating students of the middle schools under their jurisdiction, after the original school's examination of their graduation grades and determination of their eligibility, hold graduation examinations.

Article 2 The graduation examinations for public and established private middle schools in provinces, counties, and cities shall be handled by a committee organized by the educational administrative agencies of the respective provinces.

The graduation examinations for public (excluding those established by the province) and established private middle schools in cities (municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan) and districts (special administrative regions) shall be handled by a committee organized by the educational administrative agencies of the respective cities and districts. Article 3 The regulations for the graduation examination committee for middle school students shall be separately determined by the Ministry's order.

Article 4 The subjects for the examination are tentatively set as follows:

1. Senior High School: Civics, Chinese, Mathematics, Physics, Chemistry, Biology, History, Geography, Foreign Language.

2. Junior High School: Civics, Chinese, Mathematics, Physics and Chemistry, Biology (Zoology and Botany), History and Geography, Foreign Language.

Article 5 The semester examinations for the second semester of the third year for the graduating students of the schools participating in the examination should be held within two weeks before the date of the examination.

Article 6 One month before the examination, each school shall submit a roster with photos of graduating students to the competent educational administrative agency, and the graduation grade reports for each subject shall also be submitted before the start of the examination.

Article 7 The method for calculating the grades for each subject in the graduation examination should be based on the school's graduation grades for each subject (i.e., the average of the grades for the three years) accounting for 40% and the examination grades for each subject accounting for 60%, which are combined for calculation.

The grades mentioned above should be calculated using the percentage method, and 60 points should be used as the passing standard.

Article 8 The graduation examinations in various regions should be held within the last week of June and the first week of January each year. The location of the examination shall be determined and announced by the competent educational administrative agency. In areas with a wider area and a large number of students, the examination should be conducted in different areas for the convenience of students, but it must still be held in accordance with the prescribed dates.

The questions used in the examination shall be determined by the question-setting committee of the examination committee, and the test papers shall be prepared and sealed by the competent educational administrative agency.

Article 9 Students must pass all subjects in the graduation examination to graduate. The graduation certificate shall be issued by the school after being stamped by the provincial or municipal educational administrative agency and affixed with the "Graduation Examination Passed" seal.

Article 10 Those who fail in three or more subjects in the examination should be ordered to repeat the grade. Those who cannot repeat the grade due to special reasons may be given a certificate of completion by the original school, stating the grades of each subject in the graduation examination, and affixing the "Graduation Examination Failed" seal.

Article 11 Those who fail in one or two subjects in the examination shall be allowed to continue to participate in two graduation examinations of various subjects for two sessions. Only after passing can they graduate. If there are still subjects that fail, they should take the examination for all subjects. During the examination, those who are unable to take all or part of the examination subjects due to special reasons will be considered failing in the missing subjects.

Article 12 Students who fail in one or two subjects in the examination and wish to continue their studies may have the competent educational administrative agency issue a certificate for taking the entrance examination for further education, stating the grades of each subject in the graduation examination, allowing them to take the entrance examination for further education first. After being admitted, they will be regarded as probationary students. Only after participating in the examination for each subject and passing, and after obtaining a graduation certificate, will they be allowed to participate in the graduation examination of the school they have entered.

Article 13 If students who fail in one or two subjects in the examination go to other provinces or cities for further study or service, the student may ask the original school to request the competent educational administrative agency to request the competent educational administrative agency in the location where the student is studying or serving to allow them to participate in the local graduation examination and take the examination for each subject.

Article 14 The educational administrative agencies of each province, city, and district shall announce the results of the examination within one week after the examination and issue graduation examination passing certificates.

Article 15 At the end of the examination, the average of the grades of each subject obtained by each student shall be disclosed separately in grades. At the same time, the percentage of the number of graduating students from each school to the number of participants shall be listed as A, B, C, and D grades, and then the average of the grades of the students who passed the examination from each school shall be listed as A, B, C, and D grades for disclosure.

Article 16 The ranking of graduating students in each school must be arranged by the competent educational administrative agency according to the graduation examination grades of each student in each subject.

Article 17 Before holding the middle school graduation examination, the educational administrative agencies of each province, city, and district should report the location of the examination, the list of members of the inspection committee, and the procedures for holding the examination to the Ministry of Education for record, and should report the student examination grades and the preparation process of the schools participating in the examination to the record within one month after the end of the examination.

Article 18 The educational administrative agencies of each province, city, and district must be strict in guarding against fraud when holding the examination. If there is any leakage of test questions or other fraud, they should be punished according to law.

Article 19 The educational administrative agencies of each province, city, and district should strictly examine the school graduation grades of each student participating in the examination. If any fraud is found, the whole or part of the grades should be denied, and the responsible personnel should be disciplined.

Article 20 If there are special difficulties for the graduating students of the junior high schools under the jurisdiction of the educational administrative agencies of each province, the Ministry of Education may, with the approval of the Ministry of Education, extract a part of the junior high schools in the province to hold the examination. However, the number of schools selected for this examination must account for more than half of the total number of junior high schools in the province.

Article 21 These Regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. Tao Xisheng attends a speech

Chinese Meteorological Society Holds Tenth Anniversary Commemorative Meeting Yesterday Annual Meeting Held in the Afternoon and Closed in the Evening 185

(Nanjing, 7th) The tenth anniversary commemorative meeting of the Chinese Meteorological Society was held at the Meteorological Institute on the morning of the 7th. More than 40 members attended. Zhu Kezhen chaired the meeting and delivered an opening speech. Zhuge Qi reported on the society's affairs. Gao Lu and Jiang Bingran delivered speeches one after another. The chairman then announced the election by correspondence. As a result, Zhu Kezhen was elected as the president, Jiang Bingran as the vice president, and the board of directors was established in Beijing. Hu Xiyong and eight others were elected as directors, and Zhuge Ying was elected as the secretary general. At the end, new members were introduced. Then, proposals were discussed, totaling 26 items, of which 22 items were handed over to the joint meeting of meteorological agencies on the 8th for discussion. The remaining four items were all related to meteorological publications and were handed over to the board of directors for handling. At noon, a lunch was held at the Central University. In the afternoon at 2:00 p.m., the annual meeting was moved to the Central University, and 10 papers were read. The evening was hosted by the Meteorological Institute to entertain the members of the congress, and then the meeting was closed.

英鎊前途之推測  冷波

Speculation on the Future of the British Pound by Leng Bo

在過去半年中，英鎊呈鬆弱之勢，以美元而言，由五·一〇元跌至四·八五元，以法郎而言，由七六·二五法郎跌至七三法郎。惟其跌落的步調，並非一致，時而緊張，時而弛緩，此乃因其所遭受的各種影響有所不同故也。如去年秋季對於美元的收買，去年十一月間金集團之政治與金融的紊亂，以及最近美國金條欺案尚未宣判以前的凌亂等是，英鎊之價值在此半年中僅跌百分之四，故較稱穩定。然而尚引起不良的批評，而金鎊在歐陸各令融中心在不久以前，亦失其信仰。

In the past six months, the British pound has shown a weakening trend, falling from $5.10 to $4.85 in terms of the U.S. dollar, and from 76.25 francs to 73 francs in terms of the French franc. However, the pace of the decline has not been consistent, sometimes tight and sometimes relaxed, due to the different influences it has been subjected to. These include the purchase of U.S. dollars last autumn, the political and financial turmoil of the gold bloc last November, and the recent chaos before the verdict in the U.S. gold bar fraud case. The value of the British pound has only fallen by 4% in the past six months, so it is relatively stable. However, it has still attracted negative criticism, and the gold pound has also lost its credibility in various European financial centers not long ago.

欲找出最近英鎊跌落的根本原因，實非易事。據英國貿易局（Board　of　Trade）最近的估計，英國國際收支的不利差額僅為一百萬鎊，此種估計固難精確，但是耶使在英國有利的方面再多估出一二千萬鎊，而常此資金大量移動中的今日，其所估計之不利差額之數目，亦不足為影響鎊價主要的原因。再據一月份之貿易報吿所示，英國之貿易地位並未退步，其貿易不利差額，亦較去年同期减少。至於英鎊之購買力，若與一年前或去年八月間之法郎及美元的購買力相較，則英鎊以美元而言。其價值尚為高估，但最後美國物價之高漲及鎊滙之縮短，則此項價值的為估，遂歸消滅；惟以法郎而言，英鎊之價值，仍為低估，其低估之程度雖較八月間者稍大，但僅抵去年二月間者三分之二。

It is not easy to find the root cause of the recent fall in the British pound. According to the recent estimates of the British Board of Trade, the unfavorable balance of the British international payments is only one million pounds. Although such estimates are difficult to be accurate, even if the favorable aspects of the British side are overestimated by ten or twenty million pounds, the estimated amount of unfavorable differences is insufficient to be the main reason for affecting the pound price in today's large-scale movement of funds. Furthermore, according to the trade report in January, the trade position of the United Kingdom has not deteriorated, and its trade imbalance has also decreased compared with the same period last year. As for the purchasing power of the British pound, compared with the purchasing power of the franc and the U.S. dollar a year ago or in August last year, the value of the British pound is still overestimated in terms of the U.S. dollar, but the final surge in U.S. prices and the shortening of the pound exchange rate have eliminated this value's estimation; however, in terms of the franc, the value of the British pound is still underestimated, although the degree of undervaluation is slightly larger than that in August, but only two-thirds of that in February last year.

吾人甚易誤視美元價值的低估與法郎價值的高估，其中間之差別是使英鎊跌落的主因。實則些三種貨幣間之差異，自去年起已大為减少也。且此種差異，即使無英鎊的跌價，亦可有同樣之减少。蓋因美元與法郎間的平衡已日趨接近，而英鎊在此二幣間所處之地位，則須由其本身的特殊因素而决定耳。其决定之原因究竟如何？有如下文所述：

It is easy for us to mistakenly view the undervaluation of the U.S. dollar and the overvaluation of the French franc, and the difference between them as the main reason for the fall of the British pound. In fact, the difference between these three currencies has been greatly reduced since last year. Moreover, this difference can be reduced in the same way even without the depreciation of the British pound, because the balance between the U.S. dollar and the French franc is getting closer, and the position of the British pound between these two currencies must be determined by its own special factors. What are the reasons for the decision? The following is described:

首先吾人須知英鎊與各種金幣（美元亦包括在內）間的關係，不僅是受英國國內的貿易情形所決定，而亦受英鎊集團整個酌貿易情形所決定。倘英帝國（包含加拿大澳洲南非等在內）阿根庭及其他金幣國家間的貿易衰落，而英鎊集團內部的滙兌率仍無變更時，則此種壓迫，即不免於英鎊滙價上表現。在英國的各統治邦中其地位亦有不如一年前的强固者，例如澳洲羊毛出口價值之縮减，即其一端。其次吾人對於倫敦與其他各國金融的中心的利息水準，亦應加以注意。英國政府所採行的低利政策Cheap　Money　Rolicy　,使短期利率降至最抵之紀錄。長期者亦降至三厘以下，實較巴黎現行之利率為低，但其低於紐約者之程度不若低於巴黎者之甚，按正統經濟學派的理論，倫敦資金將自然流入巴黎，吾人對於此種解釋，須

First of all, we must know that the relationship between the British pound and various gold coins (including the U.S. dollar) is not only determined by the domestic trade situation in the United Kingdom, but also by the entire trade situation of the British pound bloc. If trade between the British Empire (including Canada, Australia, South Africa, etc.), Argentina, and other gold coin countries declines, and the exchange rate within the British pound bloc remains unchanged, then this pressure will inevitably be reflected in the pound exchange rate. The position of the British dominions is also less strong than it was a year ago, such as the reduction in the export value of Australian wool, which is one aspect. Secondly, we should also pay attention to the interest rate levels of London and other financial centers in various countries. The cheap money policy adopted by the British government has reduced the short-term interest rate to the lowest record. Long-term rates have also fallen below 3%, which is lower than the current interest rate in Paris, but the extent to which it is lower than that in New York is not as great as that in Paris. According to the theory of the orthodox economics school, London funds will naturally flow into Paris. We must

第一為存於倫敦之外幣的數量問題，其準確數目，吾人不得而知，但可得而言者，為較一九三一年恐慌發生以前為少。倫敦之情况，固較四年前為鞏固。但倘政府不加干涉，即不甚激烈之提欵，亦可使其滙價跌落。吾人更應加以注意者，為倫敦與巴黎間短期利率之差額，久與遠期法郎的貼現相抵，蓋該貼現即至今日，仍等於年利一厘半也。是以法國銀行現在收買英國庫券（Treasury　Bill）可賺利二厘，興能，則英國之投資家對於在歐陸的長期投資，常取審愼之態度，固不僅視利息之厚薄而已也

First, there is the issue of the amount of foreign currency stored in London. We cannot know the exact number, but what we can say is that it is less than before the panic in 1931. The situation in London is certainly more solid than it was four years ago. However, if the government does not intervene, even a not-so-drastic withdrawal of funds can cause its exchange rate to fall. What we should pay more attention to is the difference between the short-term interest rates in London and Paris, which has long been offset by the discount on forward francs, because that discount is still equal to an annual interest rate of 1.5% even today. Therefore, French banks can now earn a 2% profit by buying British Treasury Bills. Therefore, British investors often take a cautious attitude towards long-term investments in Europe, not only considering the thickness of interest rates.

此外吾人對於心理上的形態，亦應加以注意。蓋當此他國資金大量兼容避之際，心理作用甚關重要。約於三星期前，外人對於英鎊之信心，因種種原因，突受搖撼。其原恩呢如樹脂與胡椒投機之失敗，而使國外金融受極大之影響。更甚者如因Wavertree地方的選舉與失業協助的計劃而造成政府行將改組及普選先期舉行之種利謠言；而其發生適當關於金集國各國幣制穩定與否的謠言叢生之時，故產生一種疑慮之觀念。念其觀為：凡一種不穩定之貨幣有時必將跌落，英國，欲一方採行無限制的低利政策，而同時又希望維持其鎊的穩定，實不可能

In addition, we should also pay attention to the psychological form. Because when other countries' funds are highly compatible and avoid, the psychological effect is very important. About three weeks ago, foreigners' confidence in the British pound was suddenly shaken for various reasons. The original gracefulness is like the failure of resin and pepper speculation, which has a great impact on foreign finance. Even more so, the rumors that the government will be reorganized and general elections will be held in advance due to the election in Wavertree and the unemployment assistance plan; and its occurrence is appropriate when rumors about the stability of the currency system of the gold collective countries are rampant, so a concept of doubt arises. Reading it is that: any unstable currency will inevitably fall sometimes. It is impossible for the United Kingdom to adopt an unrestricted low-interest policy on the one hand, while hoping to maintain the stability of its pound.

此種心理上的原因，或為暫時的現象，但實予吾人一種警吿。是時英國政府證券適大漲價，而外國投資者，對英國在議會的生命能否持久，方有疑問。是以許多外國投資家，以為現在為拋資英國證券最宜之時，以便獲利，而將其資金再運還本國。對於工黨將來得權之推測，無論其為正確，或為錯誤，皆足減少英鎊之信用。該黨對於凡已經林用過的各種金本位皆拒絕復用，並希望用國際的動作以穩定滙兌，簡言之，該黨之方策尚未確定，然而其引起外人對於英鎊不信任之處，由於其貨幣政策者少，而由於其增加歲出所生之恐慌則更多也，故此種疑慮。只有該黨領袖始能使其消散。

This psychological reason may be a temporary phenomenon, but it actually gives us a warning. At that time, British government securities rose sharply, and foreign investors questioned whether the United Kingdom's life in parliament could last. Therefore, many foreign investors thought that now was the best time to throw British securities in order to make profits and transport their funds back to their home countries. Speculation about the Labour Party's future accession to power, whether correct or wrong, is sufficient to reduce the credit of the British pound. The party refuses to reuse all kinds of gold standards that have been used in the past, and hopes to use international actions to stabilize exchange rates. In short, the party's strategy has not yet been determined. However, the distrust of foreigners in the British pound is less due to its monetary policy and more due to the panic caused by its increased expenditure. Therefore, this doubt. Only the party leader can dispel it.

同時吾人所欲問者，為英鎊跌價是否易生有害之影響？英鎊每跌落一次，即增加金集團之困難一次，而上漲則為該團所歡迎，然英鎊的價值縱有最近之跌落，但若與一般貨幣比較。尚無十分低估之象。

At the same time, what we want to ask is whether the depreciation of the British pound is likely to have a harmful impact? Every time the British pound falls, it increases the difficulty of the gold group by one time, and the rise is welcomed by the group, but even if the value of the British pound has fallen recently, if compared with the general currency. There is still no sign of significant undervaluation.

英鎊現狀雖不是發生恐慌，然亦不應聽其自然，凡由於投機及心理的關係而發生倫敦資金的外流，應自行抵消，蓋此種原因不合於眞正之經濟事實的情况，而不久即可自然矯正也。惟以往資金外流之所以不能抵消者，或因其當局者認為此乃資金之正當的减少，或因平準基金之來源，不足以維持此項困難工作。在第一種情形下，則不當用任何方法以停止其外流。在第二種情形下，則無方法能使其停止也。如提高銀行利率，則其擾亂國內外信用之影響，將較吸收外資流入倫敦者為甚。一九三二年至一九三三年聞所積累之現金，此時若有一部份輸出國外，尤其在此項輸出外復有外人提取倫敦之存欵時，則其為衰弱現象的表示，自較英鎊逐漸跌落者為尤顯著。

Although the current situation of the British pound is not a panic, it should not be allowed to take its course. All the outflow of London funds due to speculation and psychological relations should be offset by itself, because this reason is not in line with the true economic situation, and it will be naturally corrected soon. However, the reason why the past outflow of funds cannot be offset is either because the authorities believe that this is a legitimate reduction of funds, or because the source of the stabilization fund is insufficient to maintain this difficult work. In the first case, no methods should be used to stop the outflow. In the second case, there is no way to stop it. If the bank interest rate is raised, its impact on disrupting domestic and foreign credit will be greater than attracting foreign investment into London. If a part of the cash accumulated from 1932 to 1933 is exported abroad at this time, especially when foreigners withdraw their deposits in London after this export, it is a sign of weakness, which is more obvious than the gradual fall of the British pound.

但以上各種可能情勢，距今尚屬遼遠。現在英鎊之跌落，僅在與以前數月之穩定狀態比較而顯著。在英鎊仍未穩定，尤其是市塲仍為心理作用所波動之時，則最近數週所發生之各種現象，殆屬無可避免也。

However, the above possible situations are still far away from now. The current fall of the British pound is only significant when compared with the stable state of the previous months. When the British pound is still unstable, especially when the market is still fluctuating due to psychological effects, the various phenomena that have occurred in recent weeks are almost inevitable.

汕頭通貨制度崩潰之研討  鄧邦傑

A Study of the Collapse of the Shantou Currency System by Deng Bangjie

汕頭銀業，自前年四月廿六日迄今，遭遇絕大之風險，覆亡者幾度其半，　時之士，　言救濟，因其觀察之不同，而其主張遂亦形成兩大派：其一，以為現象所以惡劣，在乎通貨運用之不足，故主張膨脹通貨，以救目前，此之謂通貨膨脹派。一則以為市塲之騷動，在乎產業保證紙幣信用之失　，其始則主張互助聯保以維信用，故有總兌換之主張，繼則主張通貨收縮，以安人心，是謂通貨收縮

Page 22

Chewing on a certain section in his mind again and again, then calculating with his fingers, "This is the 'Month of忌 (Ji)'! This is the 'Month of忌 (Ji)'!" He raised his head, the oil stains and powder residue on the stolen small pine and locust trees seemed like the blurry flesh of his ancestors, and tears welled up! (The living lion is struggling, the mountain god is roaring, and the ancestral spirit is cursing, cursing whom? Cursing the unfilial descendants—himself!) Unfilial! What a grave sin! If I let these guys go again this time, then my whole life would be in vain, and I would truly be letting down my ancestors in the ground! So he prepared to concentrate all his accumulated anger—even the anger from the last time the ××× Association forcibly felled ancient trees—to burn He Xinye. He stroked his sparse, white beard and decided to reply to the mediator who would come in the afternoon: At the very least, there must be a firecracker ban and a mountain sealing, guaranteeing that within three years there will be no illnesses or harm to the family, otherwise, send him to jail! Angrily, he packed the compass into a small blue cloth bag, mustered his remaining strength to get up, and, leaning on a wooden cane, turned to the left side of the mountain, gently stroking the "Rhinoceros Gazing at the Moon Stone" that had been lying there for countless years. From the marks of wind and rain erosion on the stone, he thought of the current dilapidated mountain appearance and the declining human fortune, he bowed his head, and two clear tears flowed down both resentfully and secretly. Afterward, he staggered home along a small path overgrown with weeds. At lunchtime, it seemed as if the ancestors had tightened the old man's throat, and he didn't want to eat. After repeated persuasion from his wife and son, he went to the table. Just as he picked up the bowl, his hand slipped, and the bowl shattered on the ground, with rice and broken pieces scattering all over the room. "Damn it! This is not a good sign! That bastard He Xinye must be dealt with severely. Quickly, arrange the package for me!" The meal didn't happen, and his wife and son were so anxious that they kept pinching their thighs. At this moment, the mediator, Wang Tuanzong, and Cai Huzhang, the head of the household affairs, walked in. Cai Huzhang had a mouth skilled in eloquent speech. As soon as he entered, he said "久遂 (jiǔ suí)" (a polite greeting, like "I've been remiss in visiting") and inquired about the old man's health. Wang Tuanzong also followed suit with conventional greetings, which forced the old man to put on a smiling face to welcome them. After they had tea, they turned the conversation to the main topic: "He Xinye is ignorant. We've scolded him a good deal. Elder, please, for our sake, be a little lenient?" Cai Huzhang said gently. "Of course, of course! But the last time the trees on my ancestral graves were completely cut down, my eldest son died as a result. I can't be lenient this time. At the very least, there must be a firecracker ban and mountain sealing, guaranteeing that my family suffers no more harm within three years!" the old man stammered in reply. Wang Tuanzong continued, "Guarantee... we can't take on such a big responsibility." "That won't do. I'll have to send him to jail!" the old man shook his head resolutely. The atmosphere of despair pressed on them, and they took their leave of the old man with unnatural smiles. The old man called out to Kezi to quickly bring out the package. Lianjiang Shang Tuo Ren A spring countryside trip is likely to make one's mood burn with a faint warmth. It was afternoon, the sun's soft light dazzled people's eyes, leaping on the earth. When the train arrived at Longjing, the station became a bustling market town. The noisy voices of the country folk echoed in every corner around the station. Those who came out of the train platform walked along the small gravel path. After about a few hundred steps, they arrived at the pier for the steamboats going to the upper reaches of the Lianjiang River. Although Longjing Port did not have ships sailing to the open sea, nor did it have the magnificent docks of a trading port, it did have customs, a very large checkpoint. On the shore, patrolling police officers were walking with large strides, their eyes watching the passengers and their luggage boarding and disembarking as if they were thieves. The reason was that Longjing Port could directly connect to overseas. The reports often carried stories of foreigners smuggling goods into the Chaoshan area along the coast, and this was their usual route. Fierce tides rushed into the small port, tightly squeezed between the mountain peaks. The color of the water was peach red, like a red velvet blanket covering Longjing Port. When the tide receded back into the sea, the vast water surface would reveal patches of red sand and mud, as if sailing in the sea, one could see the belly of a large fish, rolling on the water's surface, shimmering with the golden light of the sun. The small steamer going to the upper reaches of the Lianjiang River departed in the afternoon. It took about an hour to enter the Lianjiang River. The water gradually changed from red to green. If one were to stand on a higher mountain peak and look down, the winding river would look like a silver chain placed on the ground, with a tranquil spring flowing from top to bottom. The water was a sheet of emerald green, without a single ripple, as smooth as a piece of glass wiped with white powder. Green bamboo thickets embraced both banks, with some branches extending into the space, closely connected, reflecting a dark shadow on the water surface. If one looked up, the vast sky and sea would become a very small Milky Way, shining in harmony with the green water below. The people sitting in the cabin, when they reached the midway point, climbed onto the deck one by one. The sound of their conversations, like the sound of the engine, reverberated through the quiet villages on both banks of the river. People in the city rarely see thatched houses in the countryside. Here, they are displayed like an exhibition, showing all kinds of houses from centuries ago. Country folk who walk across the stone bridges that have been around for hundreds of years also stare blankly at these people standing on the deck, as if saying: What's so fun about the countryside? After the boat had been traveling on the river for several hours, many dilapidated houses appeared on both banks, some tall and some short, all lying in ruins in the fields. According to the country folk on the boat, this was once a very lively village a few years ago. In recent years, droughts and floods have left it uninhabited. Country folk talk incessantly. He talked about the ruins and the fields in the wilderness. He continued, "Country folk rely on the harvest every year. You see the good green rice stalks on the shore and think the harvest must be good. But even a good year's harvest is not enough to pay off debts, so now even the people have run away, and there are far fewer farmers." The tranquil Lianjiang River, the beautiful Lianjiang River, although it irrigates countless fields, only a few receive the blessings it gives to the country folk. Farewell Hu Weixiong The night before, I chatted with the host until late at night, hearing the sound of the clapper striking three in the morning in the distance before saying good night and retiring. In the countryside, as the setting sun slants westward, smoke rises from the chimneys, as families prepare dinner. Usually, after dinner, the old lady would take a puff of her water pipe, piously offer a stick of incense before the Buddha niche, then close her eyes and wrap her string of 108 prayer beads around her left wrist, softly chanting scriptures, turning the beads in her right hand to count, completing about an hour of meritorious service. During this time, my little friend would study the characters taught by his grandmother in the morning. The child was very intelligent, and rarely made mistakes in recognizing the characters with many strokes or those that looked similar after reading them. Sometimes we would also tell stories or play with the educational six-sided pictures that his father had bought for him. Although I was a big child myself, and had learned some so-called "art of living" in the waves of life, the child and I got along very well for two months, and he didn't feel that I was older than the age of his playmate! Perhaps my precious innocence hadn't been completely swallowed up by the huge waves? During this short convalescence period, I filled two thick notebooks with diary entries, writing nearly a thousand words each day. I had abandoned this courage for a long time! Seventy percent of it recorded my experiences of wandering around with a cane, and more than 20,000 words commemorated the revival of my childlike heart. Now, I have hidden these two notebooks in my trunk. Since my trip to Xiaonv Temple, I haven't dared to visit scenic spots again. Content with what I have, I want to keep these excellent images deep in my mind, as vivid as if I were still there. Moreover, my vacation is also coming to an end, and this untethered heart will be sent back into the huge waves to be tempered! Three days ago, I told the host about my return date. The old lady, as if unwilling to see her son leave as she did in the past, planned many ways that were almost like coaxing a child to extend my stay. Having grown up being blown about by the wild wind, I almost wanted to live in the warm room of maternal love. I initially stayed at this foreign inn as a traveler, but who would have thought that when the little friend saw me off at the pier, I would shed a few clear tears, tears that I had never shed in the face of storms! Yesterday afternoon, I sorted out the books and simple luggage I had brought. The host sat by the window, burning paper offerings, and did not want to smoke a pipe. I tried my best to lower my head to avoid her gaze, but the oppressive atmosphere made the child, who was snuggled in his grandmother's lap, remain motionless for a long time. Finally, I took the child for a walk nearby, barely managing to send the sun back to the western mountains. Last night's dinner was especially lavish. The host even urged me to drink wine infused with rose petals. I drank three glasses without knowing why, and didn't feel drunk at all. Normally, I would probably have been unconscious long ago. After dinner, when the child brought out his character box, the host told him to play with his building blocks instead, and started chatting with me, holding her water pipe and rambling on. The host was usually talkative, but yesterday she kept repeating old stories more than twice, and kept lighting up paper offerings, forgetting even the ritual of offering incense to the Buddha. Huang Ma occasionally peeked from behind the door, perhaps surprised by the abnormal behavior of us, the host and guest? I was unusually excited and completely forgot about sleep. When I heard the sound of the clapper striking three in the morning, the host exclaimed in surprise, "What? It's three in the morning!" This ended our conversation. Back in my bedroom, I still had no desire to sleep. I took out the diary I had put in my suitcase and reviewed it until I could no longer bear the fatigue and fell asleep at my desk. In the morning, Huang Ma told me that the old lady had caught a cold last night and couldn't get out of bed today, so she asked her grandson to see me off at the pier. I really wanted to go to her bedroom to say goodbye, but I keenly thought that what if the host was sitting there smoking her water pipe perfectly well? So I asked Huang Ma to convey my farewell and left the home of this warm friend, which had felt like home for the past two months! Supplement to the "Shen Bao" Local Edition Movie Special Issue Lowly Origins of Famous European and American Directors Zhu Heng Directors can be considered the most important job in the film industry. It requires life experience and knowledge of all production departments. Many famous European and American directors have struggled their way up from humble occupations. Even many of today's top directors did not originally come from the film industry. Some were only engaged in stage comedy, and there is no shortage of people who have never even worked in theater. Ernst Lubitsch, the big name, was a comedian in Berlin as far back as 1913. Because he felt that the plays he was performing lacked suitable material, he decided to write his own scripts and take on the role of director. That attempt was successful, and the company trusted him, assigning him to write, direct, and star in a two-reel comedy short film. Later, when he directed Pola Negri's "Carmen," he abandoned short films and became a director of comedies. Frank Capra used to be a comedian at Hal Roach and Mack Sennett's film companies, which specialized in producing slapstick short films. When the famous comedian Harry Langdon decided to act in a feature film, he hired Capra to direct "The Strong Man," and this debut work was selected as one of the top ten films of 1926. Walter Forde, the British director of "Rome Express" and the anti-Chinese film "Jack Ahoy," used to be a musician in an orchestra. After the war, he invested all his savings in the film industry. As a result, he directed a comedy short film. Although he unfortunately went bankrupt, he later became famous for directing a feature film called "Would You Believe It?" Frank Borzage started out directing American Westerns. Later, he gradually transformed into a famous master of sentimental romance films. His famous works include "Seventh Heaven" and "Man's Castle," etc. Cecil B. DeMille's first work was "The Squaw Man" ("The Trail of the Lonesome Pine"). This was the first film produced in Hollywood in 1913. That same year was also when he and Jesse L. Lasky began to found Paramount Pictures. Frank Lloyd was also a pioneer in the film industry. In 1913, he only played a bit part actor in "Shadows of Life." Later, he became a screenwriter and director of short films. Dorothy Arzner is one of the few female directors in Hollywood. Before becoming a director, she was just a film editor. Later, she gained the company's trust and became a director. Her debut work was "Fashions for Women." George Cukor can be considered a rising star among many contemporary directors. His masterpiece is "Little Women." His debut work was "The Royal Family of Broadway." Undoubtedly, it was most appropriate for him to direct this film, because he was a famous stage manager in New York. In fact, "The Royal Family of Broadway" was not his first job, because he had already written a lot of dialogue for "All Quiet on the Western Front." Victor Saville, the director of the British blockbuster "The Dictator," was a film dealer before the war. Later, he directed an advertising film for an American oil company, thus beginning his film career. The first film he officially directed was a silent film called "Woman to Woman." Rene Clair, the famous French director, was a journalist before entering the film industry in 1922. His debut work was "The Crazy Ray," and his famous masterpiece was "The Italian Straw Hat." G.W. Pabst, the famous German director of literary films "Don Quixote," "Kameradschaft," and "The White Hell of Piz Palü," became famous after directing the Greta Garbo-starring "The Joyless Street" in Germany. Movie Review of "A Flower on Peng Island" You Jing "Red Morning"—Grand Shanghai Theater A film mainly set against the warm wind and waves of the South China Sea and the beautiful scenery of Peng Island, it can be said to satisfy the entertainment desires of gentlemen who are tired of writing in the office and tired of the dance halls and brothels. It is more like a reflection of the desire of people who are suffocated by gold and goods, hoping to rediscover some new island where they can make a difference. This can be seen from "Fragrant Sea," "Peng Island Spring," "Pearl Island," "The Adventures of an Adventuress," and the currently showing "A Flower on Peng Island." Although these films do not seem to make explicit expressions subjectively or directly, it is obvious that they are consciously or unconsciously adapting to these requirements. For example, "A Flower on Peng Island" seems to be expressing a didactic story about how bad people will eventually destroy themselves under the guise of love, but in its devoted depiction of the life of aborigines on the barren island of the South China Sea, it clearly hints at this way out. For example, the playwright makes the daughter of the shipowner, Bai Laisha, giving the aborigines a water injection, and saving the chairman's son, Mayo, from death, as the main key, in order to show that she obtained the qualifications of a distinguished guest from the status of a prisoner. It also emphasized that setting off fireworks was enough to scare away thousands of armed aborigines, that Karan single-handedly rescued her lover, John, who was about to be burned by the aborigines, and that Karan only needed to strike a board to make a sound, which was passed on by the aborigines' watchers beating drums, and then tens of thousands of aborigines would come with spears and boats to save her, etc., all implying how easily white people could establish relationships with those aborigines on the barren islands, or that the honest and useless aborigines were eagerly awaiting civilized people to conquer them. Apart from these, we can see from the technical aspect that "A Flower on Peng Island" is not such a great work. Let's start with an analogy! The material of "A Flower on Peng Island" could have been made into a simple, elegant, and self-admiring plum blossom, but now it has been turned into a bonsai by a very mediocre gardener. But here, there are also the heavy drum sounds and simple songs and dances of the aborigines on the desert island, as well as the paintings and sounds of wild fires and lush forests. However, the necessary movements of vigor, wildness, and strength are not well expressed due to poor editing. The so-called poor editing is mainly too chaotic. For example, when describing the three parties of the aborigines helping Karan and her husband fight against the bad guy Stan Gan, it is so chaotic that it loses the due sense of urgency. Long distant shots are often used, which weakens the short, urgent melody. It should have been an extremely fast tempo after the ship was wrecked, but Karan was allowed to leisurely search for her lost father with a lamp. What is more successful is the emotional expression. On the evening before the ship wrecked, Karan's reminiscence of her father, the scenes before and after her father's death, and the separation from Mayo, all successfully touched the audience and achieved excellent results. This is not due to the successful surgery of director Wallace Fordes, but to the heroine Stephanie Dawn. Judging from her face and figure, she is really better at playing a desolate and plain role than a female hero of nautical adventure. The success and failure here is a clear proof. Real Peach Blossom River Discovered During Location Shooting A few days ago, a Tianyi film crew was shooting location scenes for "Returning Home" in the western suburbs of Shanghai. In front of the peach blossom forest, there was a small river with clear blue water and exceptionally beautiful scenery. We usually love to sing "Peach Blossom River" and always think that "Peach Blossom River" is ideal. Little did we know that the place where we are filming today is the real "Peach Blossom River"! "Rainbow Tune" Coming Soon Yunshan Cicely Courtneidge is a monster on the European stage and screen. People call her the female Chaplin. The films she has starred in that have been screened in Shanghai include "Maytime," "Almost a Honeymoon," and "Spring in the Air." These three films received very good reviews when they were first released in Shanghai. Now, we are about to see her new work "Rainbow Tune" (Aunt Sally). Like "Maytime," it is also a musical comedy. Here, Courtneidge plays a girl who is obsessed with song and dance. At first, because she was not a well-known actress, she was repeatedly rejected by the troupe leader. However, she was not discouraged and still tried her best to play the main character in the play. As the saying goes, "Where there's a will, there's a way," and she finally achieved the final victory. The entire film is organized with fresh and humorous material, and there are several song and dance scenes that are very novel and beautiful. Everything is no less than Courtneidge's previous works. It is said that it will be released at the Guanglu Theater in the coming days. Tianyi Gossips Bai Yun Gao Lihong's illness has not yet healed. Shen Yongshi had a daughter seven days ago. Xiao Zhengzhong plays a doctor in "Returning Home." Newcomers Lin Cuifang and Yu Yingjun performed in "Returning Home." According to Wang Bin, the score work for "Mother" will be completed within a few days. Among the new films planned to be filmed this year, there will be one entirely set against the "sea." Tianyi is determined to cultivate newcomers and is currently studying what kind of strategy to adopt. The songs in "Returning Home" will also be printed and distributed to all sectors. The city street scene in "Returning Home" has not yet been filmed due to rain. The song "Sunny Day" in "Returning Home" is full of poetry and extremely gentle and moving. When filming the hospital scene in "Returning Home," several doctors from Chen Mo Pediatric Hospital came to visit and were very satisfied with all the equipment and arrangements.
